DIVISION 1. - GENERALLY 

Sec. 2-61. - Provisions saved from repeal. 
The bylaws for the Cordele-Crisp County Clean and Beautiful Commission, the Crisp County Clean and Beautiful Committee and the Cordele-Crisp Clean Community Commission are not repealed and shall continue in full force and effect pending a revision of the subject matter by the county. 
Secs. 2-62—2-80. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 2. - AIRPORT BOARD[4] 

Footnotes: 
--- (4) --- 
State Law reference— Aviation, O.C.G.A. § 6-1-1 et seq.; authority to acquire, construct and maintain airports, O.C.G.A. § 6-3-20 et seq.; general powers of counties and municipalities as to airports, O.C.G.A. § 6-3-25; authority to enforce police regulations in airports, O.C.G.A. § 6-3-27. 

Sec. 2-81. - Declaration of need. 
There is declared a continuing need of an airport board to function as an advisory board to the board of commissioners. 
(Res. of 6-13-1989, § 1) 
Sec. 2-82. - Name; members. 
The airport board is renamed the Crisp County-Cordele Airport Board and shall continue to consist of not less than five nor more than seven members. Such board shall continue to choose its chairman from its members. 
(Res. of 6-13-1989, § 2) 
Editor's note— The Cordele Municipal Airport Board was created by a resolution adopted June 7, 1955. 
Sec. 2-83. - Powers and duties. 
The powers and duties of the airport board shall be to advise the board of commissioners on matters of concern at the Crisp County-Cordele Airport, including, but not limited to: 
(1)  The hiring and discharge of employees; 
(2)  The number, size and rental of hangar facilities; 
(3)  Furnishing of fuel and other service; 
(4)  Maintenance, improvement, leasing and acquisition of facilities, equipment and structures; and 
(5)  The production and implementation of plans for the development of the Crisp County-Cordele Airport. 
(Res. of 6-13-1989, § 3) 
Secs. 2-84—2-100. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 3. - DEVELOPMENT AUTHORITY[5] 

Footnotes: 
--- (5) --- 
Cross reference— Development code, app. A. 
State Law reference— Development Authorities Law, O.C.G.A. § 36-62-1 et seq.; resource Recovery Development Authorities Law, O.C.G.A. § 36-63-1 et seq.; Georgia Development Authority Act, O.C.G.A. § 50-10-1 et seq. 

Sec. 2-101. - Declaration of need; activation. 
(a)  There is determined and declared to be a pressing, existing and future need for a development authority (as more fully described and defined in the Development Authorities Law, O.C.G.A. § 36-62-1 et seq.), to function in the county for the purpose of developing and promoting for the public good and general welfare trade, commerce, industry and employment opportunities in the county thereby promoting the general welfare of the citizenry. 
(b)  There is activated in the county the public body corporate and politic known as the "development authority of the county" which is created under the adoption and approval of the Development Authorities Law, O.C.G.A. § 36-62-1 et seq. 
(Res. of 3-8-1979) 
Sec. 2-102. - Board of directors; terms. 
(a)  The board of directors of the development authority shall consist of seven members. The first members of the board of directors shall be appointed for terms of two for two years, two for four years, and three for six years. Thereafter, the terms of office of all board members shall be for six years and until their successors are elected and qualified. 
(b)  The board of directors of the development authority of the county elected pursuant to subsection (a) of this section shall organize itself, carry out its duties and responsibilities and exercise its powers and prerogatives in accordance with the terms and provisions of the Development Authorities Law, O.C.G.A. § 36-62-1 et seq., as it now exists and as it might hereafter be amended or modified. 
(Res. of 3-8-1979) 
Sec. 2-103. - Industrial development authority. 
Action taken by the board of commissioners under this division is not intended in any way to affect the Crisp County-Cordele Industrial Development Authority, including, without limitation, its existence, purpose, organization, powers or function. 
(Res. of 3-8-1979) 
Secs. 2-104—2-120. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 4. - JOINT DEVELOPMENT AUTHORITIES[6] 
Footnotes: 
--- (6) --- 
State Law reference— Development Authorities Law, O.C.G.A. § 36-62-1 et seq.; Georgia Development Authority Act, O.C.G.A. § 50-10-1 et seq. 

Subdivision A. - Crisp/Dooly Joint Development Authority 

Sec. 2-121. - Declaration of need; creation; name. 
(a)  In accordance with the provisions of the Development Authorities Law, O.C.G.A. § 36-62-1 et seq., the Boards of Commissioners of Crisp and Dooly Counties declare that there is a need for a joint development authority to function in the Crisp/Dooly County region of the state and activates and creates, jointly with other counties pursuant to O.C.G.A. § 36-62-5.1, a development authority for such region. 
(b)  The development authority activated and created in subsection (a) of this section shall be known as the Crisp/Dooly Joint Development Authority. 
(Res. of 3-1-1995, §§ 1, 2) 
Sec. 2-122. - Members; terms. 
The development authority created under this division shall consist of five members from each participating county. The five members from each county shall be appointed by the board of commissioners of such county and shall be residents of the county they represent. The terms of office of each member shall be for four years and until their successors are appointed and qualified. 
(Res. of 3-1-1995, § 3; Res. of 9-13-2005) 
Subdivision B. - Crisp-Sumter Counties Joint Development Authority 

Sec. 2-123. - Public purpose. 
The authority is created for the public purpose of promoting and expanding business, industry and trade in Crisp and Sumter Counties and to attract and support new business industry, to provide increased employment for the citizens living within the jurisdiction of the authority and to expand the ad valorem property tax base for the two counties. 
(Ord. of 2-13-2007, § 1) 
Sec. 2-124. - Board of directors. 
The authority shall be controlled by a board of directors (the "board") consisting of members as follows: 
(a)  Five members of the board shall be appointed by the Board of Commissioners for Crisp County; and 
(b)  Five members of the board shall be appointed by the Board of Commissioners for Sumter County. 
Two of the members appointed by the board of commissioners of each county shall serve an initial two-year term. The remaining members shall serve an initial four-year term and all subsequent members appointed to the board shall serve four-year terms. Each member appointed to the board shall be a taxpayer residing within the county making the appointment to the board. The members of the board shall receive no compensation for their services, but shall be entitled to reimbursement for actual expenses incurred in the performance of their duties as members of the board. The initial members appointed by each respective county to the board shall be named in the activating concurrent resolutions approved by the board of commissioners of the two counties and attached as Exhibits "A" and "B" to the ordinance from which this section derived. Each member of the board shall serve his or her stated term noted in the resolution(s) and continue to serve as a member of the board until his or her successor is qualified and chosen. In the event of the death or resignation of a member of the board, his or her successor shall be duly appointed by the respective board of commissioners of the county where the former member was a resident. 
(Ord. of 2-13-2007, § 2) 
Sec. 2-125. - Officers. 
At the initial meeting of the board, there shall be elected by majority vote, a chairman, vice-chairman, secretary and treasurer for the authority, all of whom shall serve a one-year term. The chairman or the vice-chairman shall sign, on behalf of the authority, all official documents which shall be attested to by either the secretary or the treasurer. All resolutions of the board binding the authority to any legal obligation must be approved by a majority vote of the members of the board. 
(Ord. of 2-13-2007, § 3) 
Sec. 2-126. - Staff. 
The authority shall have authority to hire an executive director who will act as chief operating officer of the authority. The executive director shall serve as secretary of the authority and shall hire all staff, be responsible for the annual work plan and budget creation. 
(Ord. of 2-13-2007, § 4) 
Sec. 2-127. - Term. 
The authority shall be deemed formally created and authorized to do business upon the filing with the Secretary of State of these articles of organization with supporting resolutions from the two counties, attached as Exhibits "A" and "B" to the ordinance from which this section derived. The authority shall have perpetual existence but may be dissolved at any time by a two-thirds vote of the members of the board. 
(Ord. of 2-13-2007, § 5) 
Sec. 2-128. - Taxation. 
The authority shall not be required to pay any state and local taxes or other assessments imposed by the state, or any county, municipal corporation or other political subdivision or taxing district, nor shall there be any ad valorem property taxing district, nor shall there be any ad valorem property taxes assessed against any property acquired and owned by the authority or under its jurisdiction, control, possession, supervision or leased to a private entity, as provided by O.C.G.A. § 36-62-3. The foregoing exemption from taxes shall not include an exemption from sales and use taxes on property purchased by or used by the authority. 
(Ord. of 2-13-2007, § 6) 
Sec. 2-129. - Powers of the authority. 
The authority shall have all powers provided for under O.C.G.A. § 36-62-6, including, but not limited to, the power: 
(a)  To bring and defend action; 
(b)  To adopt and amend a corporate seal; 
(c)  To make and execute contracts and other instruments necessary to exercise the powers of the authority, any of which contracts may be made with the county in which the authority is located or with any one or more municipal corporations in such county; 
(d)  To receive and administer gifts, grants and devises of any property and to administer trust; 
(e)  To acquire, by purchase, gift or construction, any real or personal property desired to be acquired as part of any project or for the purpose of improving, extending, adding to, reconstructing, renovating, or remodeling any project or part thereof already acquired or for the purpose of demolition to make room for such project or any part thereof; 
(f)  To sell, lease, exchange, transfer, assign, pledge, mortgage, dispose of, or grant options for any real or personal property or interest therein for any such purposes; 
(g)  To dispose of any real property for fair market value, regardless of prior development of such property as a project, whenever the board may deem such disposition to be in the best interests of the authority if the board prior to such disposition shall determine that such real property no longer can be used advantageously as a project for the development of trade, commerce, industry and employment opportunities; 
(h)  To mortgage, convey, pledge or assign any properties, revenues, income, toll, charges, or fees owned or received by the authority; 
(i)  To extend credit or make loans to any person, firm, corporation, or other industrial entity for the planning, design, construction, acquisition or carrying out of any project, which credit or loans shall be secured by loan agreements, mortgages, security agreements, contracts and all other instruments, fees or charges, upon such terms and conditions as the authority shall determine reasonable in connection with such loans, including provision for the establishment and maintenance of reserves and insurance funds; and, in the exercise of powers granted by O.C.G.A. § 36-62-6 in connection with a project for such person, firm, corporation, or other industrial entity to require the inclusion in any contract, loan, agreement, security agreement, or other instrument, of such provisions for guaranty, insurance, construction, use, operation, maintenance and financing of a project as the authority may deem necessary or desirable; 
(j)  To acquire, accept or retain equitable interest, security interests, or other interest in any property, real or personal, by mortgage, assignment, security agreement, pledge, conveyance, contract lien, loan agreement, or other consensual transfer, in order to secure the repayment of any money loaned or credit extended by the authority; 
(k)  To construct, acquire, own, repair, remodel, maintain, extend, improve and equip projects located on land owned or leased by the authority or land owned or leased by others and to pay all or part of the cost of any such project from the proceeds of revenue bonds of the authority or from any contribution or loans by persons, firms, or corporations or any other contribution, all of which the authority is authorized to receive, accept and use; 
(l)  To borrow money and issue its revenue bonds and bond anticipation notes from time to time and to use the proceeds thereof for the purpose of paying all or part of the cost of any project, including the cost of extending, adding to or improving the project, or for the purpose of refunding any such bonds of the authority theretofore issued and to otherwise carry out the purposes for which the authority was created and to pay all other costs of the authority incident to or necessary and appropriate to such purposes, including the providing of funds to be paid into any fund or funds to secure such bonds and notes, provided that all such bonds and notes shall be issued in accordance with the procedures and subject to the limitations set forth in O.C.G.A. § 36-62-8; 
(m)  As security for repayment of authority obligations, to pledge, mortgage, convey, assign, hypothecate or otherwise encumber any property, real or personal, of the authority and to execute any trust agreement, indenture or security agreement containing any provisions not in conflict with law, which trust agreement, indenture or security agreement may provide for foreclosure or forced sale of any property of the authority upon default, on such obligations, either in payment or principal or interest or in the performance of any term or condition, as are contained in such agreement or indenture; 
(n)  To expend for the promotion of industry, agriculture and trade within its jurisdiction any funds of the authority determined by the board to be in excess of those needed for the other corporate purposes of the authority. 
(Ord. of 2-13-2007, § 7) 
Sec. 2-130. - Limitations of the authority and prohibited transactions. 
The authority shall be prohibited from directly owning or operating a project, except for an industrial park, as provided under O.C.G.A. § 36-62-7, and all members of the board shall be prohibited from transacting business for pecuniary gain with the authority, as provided by O.C.G.A. § 36-62-5(e) with such exceptions as provided therein. 
(Ord. of 2-13-2007, § 8) 
Sec. 2-131. - Job tax credits. 
The authority shall be able to take advantage of tax credits as outlined in O.C.G.A. §§ 48-7-40 and 36-62-5.1. Each county shall be able to offer its credit plus $500.00. 
(Ord. of 2-13-2007, § 9) 
Sec. 2-132. - Authority to create a multicounty business/industrial park. 
Acting as an agent for the counties involved, the authority may create a multicounty business/industrial park as allowed under Amendment 1 to the Georgia Constitution passed by the citizens November 6, 1994. The counties will enter into a single contract relating the expenses and tax sharing no matter in which county the park is located. 
(Ord. of 2-13-2007, § 10) 
Sec. 2-133. - Debt. 
The authority shall not be authorized to create in any manner any debt, liability or obligation against the State of Georgia, Crisp or Sumter Counties or any municipal corporation located therein. 
(Ord. of 2-13-2007, § 11) 
Sec. 2-134. - Bonds. 
The authority shall be entitled to issue bonds, bond anticipation notes, trust indentures, deed to secure obligations, security agreements and mortgages as provided under the provisions of O.C.G.A. § 36-62-8, subject to the limitations of O.C.G.A. § 36-63-9. 
(Ord. of 2-13-2007, § 12) 
Sec. 2-135. - Dissolution. 
If for any reason the separate corporate existence of the authority is terminated and dissolved, any and all property owned by the authority shall be transferred and assigned to the host county wherein the property is located. 
(Ord. of 2-13-2007, § 13) 
Sec. 2-136. - Amendment. 
The board, by majority vote, shall have the right to amend these articles of organization, so long as such amendment does not violate any of the provisions of the Development Authority Law for the State of Georgia, as referenced herein. 
(Ord. of 2-13-2007, § 14) 
Subdivision C. - Crisp-Turner Counties Joint Development Authority 

Sec. 2-137. - Public purpose. 
The authority is created for the public purpose of promoting and expanding business, industry and trade in Crisp and Turner Counties and to attract and support new business industry, to provide increased employment for the citizens living within the jurisdiction of the authority and to expand the ad valorem property tax base for the two counties. 
(Res. of 11-10-2009, § 1) 
Sec. 2-138. - Board of directors. 
The authority shall be controlled by a board of directors (the "board") consisting of members as follows: 
(a)  Five members of the board shall be appointed by the Board of Commissioners for Crisp County; and 
(b)  Five members of the board shall be appointed by the Board of Commissioners for Turner County. 
Two of the members appointed by the board of commissioners of each county shall serve an initial two-year term. The remaining members shall serve an initial four-year term and all subsequent members appointed to the board shall serve four-year terms. Each member appointed to the board shall be a taxpayer residing within the county making the appointment to the board. The members of the board shall receive no compensation for their services, but shall be entitled to reimbursement for actual expenses incurred in the performance of their duties as members of the board. Each member of the board shall serve his or her stated term and continue to serve as a member of the board until his or her successor is qualified and chosen. In the event of the death or resignation of a member of the board, his or her successor shall be duly appointed by the respective board of commissioners of the county where the former member was a resident. 
(Res. of 11-10-2009, § 2) 
Sec. 2-139. - Officers. 
At the initial meeting of the board, there shall be elected by majority vote, a chairman, vice-chairman, secretary and treasurer for the authority, all of whom shall serve a one-year term. The chairman or the vice-chairman shall sign, on behalf of the authority, all official documents which shall be attested to by either the secretary or the treasurer. All resolutions of the board binding the authority to any legal obligation must be approved by a majority vote of the members of the board. 
(Res. of 11-10-2009, § 3) 
Sec. 2-140. - Staff. 
The authority shall have authority to hire an executive director who will act as chief operating officer of the authority. The executive director shall serve as secretary of the authority and shall hire all staff, be responsible for the annual work plan and budget creation. 
(Res. of 11-10-2009, § 4) 
Sec. 2-140.1. - Term. 
The authority shall be deemed formally created and authorized to do business upon the filing with the Secretary of State of the supporting resolutions from the two counties, attached as Exhibits "A" and "B" to the ordinance from which this section derived. The authority shall have perpetual existence but may be dissolved at any time by a two-thirds vote of the members of the board and in conformance with O.C.G.A. § 36-62-14. 
(Res. of 11-10-2009, § 5) 
Sec. 2-140.2. - Taxation. 
The authority shall not be required to pay any state and local taxes or other assessments imposed by the state, or any county, municipal corporation or other political subdivision or taxing district, nor shall there be any ad valorem property taxing district, nor shall there be any ad valorem property taxes assessed against any property acquired and owned by the authority or under its jurisdiction, control, possession, supervision or leased to a private entity, as provided by O.C.G.A. § 36-62-3. The foregoing exemption from taxes shall not include an exemption from sales and use taxes on property purchased by or used by the authority. 
(Res. of 11-10-2009, § 6) 
Sec. 2-140.3. - Powers of the authority. 
The authority shall have all powers provided for under O.C.G.A. § 36-62-6, including, but not limited to, the power: 
(a)  To bring and defend action; 
(b)  To adopt and amend a corporate seal; 
(c)  To make and execute contracts and other instruments necessary to exercise the powers of the authority, any of which contracts may be made with the county in which the authority is located or with any one or more municipal corporations in such county; 
(d)  To receive and administer gifts, grants and devises of any property and to administer trust; 
(e)  To acquire, by purchase, gift or construction, any real or personal property desired to be acquired as part of any project or for the purpose of improving, extending, adding to, reconstructing, renovation, or remodeling any project or part thereof already acquired or for the purpose of demolition to make room for such project or any part thereof; 
(f)  To sell, lease, exchange, transfer, assign, pledge, mortgage, dispose of, or grant options for any real or personal property or interest therein for any such purposes; 
(g)  To dispose of any real property for fair market value, regardless of prior development of such property as a project, whenever the board may deem such disposition to be in the best interests of the authority if the board prior to such disposition shall determine that such real property no longer can be used advantageously as a project for the development of trade, commerce, industry and employment opportunities; 
(h)  To mortgage, convey, pledge or assign any properties, revenues, income, toll, charges, or fees owned or received by the authority; 
(i)  To extend credit or make loans to any person, firm, corporation, or other industrial entity for the planning, design, construction, acquisition or carrying out of any project, which credit or loans shall be secured by loan agreements, mortgages, security agreements, contracts and all other instruments, fees or charges, upon such terms and conditions as the Authority shall determine reasonable in connection with such loans, including provision for the establishment and maintenance of reserves and insurance funds; and, in the exercise of powers granted by O.C.G.A. § 36-62-6 in connection with a project for such person, firm, corporation, or other industrial entity to require the inclusion in any contract, loan, agreement, security agreement, or other instrument, of such provisions for guaranty, insurance, construction, use, operation, maintenance and financing of a project as the authority may deem necessary or desirable; 
(j)  To acquire, accept or retain equitable interest, security interests, or other interest in any property, real or personal, by mortgage, assignment, security agreement, pledge, conveyance, contract lien, loan agreement, or other consensual transfer, in order to secure the repayment of any money loaned or credit extended by the authority; 
(k)  To construct, acquire, own, repair, remodel, maintain, extend, improve and equip projects located on land owned or leased by the authority or land owned or leased by others and to pay all or part of the cost of any such project from the proceeds of revenue bonds of the authority or from any contribution or loans by persons, firms, or corporations or any other contribution, all of which the Authority is authorized to receive, accept and use; 
(l)  To borrow money and issue its revenue bonds and bond anticipation notes from time to time and to use the proceeds thereof for the purpose of paying all or part of the cost of any project, including the cost of extending, adding to or improving the project, or for the purpose of refunding any such bonds of the authority theretofore issued and to otherwise carry out the purposes for which the authority was created and to pay all other costs of the authority incident to or necessary and appropriate to such purposes, including the providing of funds to be paid into any fund or funds to secure such bonds and notes, provided that all such bonds and notes shall be issued in accordance with the procedures and subject to the limitations set forth in O.C.G.A. § 36-62-8; 
(m)  As security for repayment of authority obligations, to pledge, mortgage, convey, assign, hypothecate or otherwise encumber any property, real or personal, of the authority and to execute any trust agreement, indenture or security agreement containing any provisions not in conflict with law, which trust agreement, indenture or security agreement may provide for foreclosure or forced sale of any property of the authority upon default, on such obligations, either in payment or principal or interest or in the performance of any term or condition, as are contained in such agreement or indenture; 
(n)  To expend for the promotion of industry, agriculture and trade within its jurisdiction any funds of the authority determined by the board to be in excess of those needed for the other corporate purposes of the authority. 
(Res. of 11-10-2009, § 7) 
Sec. 2-140.4. - Limitations of the authority and prohibited transactions. 
The authority shall be prohibited from directly owning or operating a project, except for an industrial park, as provided under O.C.G.A. § 36-62-7, and all members of the board shall be prohibited from transacting business for pecuniary gain with the authority, as provided by O.C.G.A. § 36-62-5(e) with such exceptions as provided therein. 
(Res. of 11-10-2009, § 8) 
Sec. 2-140.5. - Job tax credits. 
The authority shall be able to take advantage of tax credits as outlined in O.C.G.A. §§ 48-7-40 and 36-62-5.1. 
(Res. of 11-10-2009, § 9) 
Sec. 2-140.6. - Debt. 
The authority shall not be authorized to create in any manner any debt, liability or obligation against the State of Georgia, Crisp or Turner Counties or any municipal corporation located therein. 
(Res. of 11-10-2009, § 10) 
Sec. 2-140.7. - Bonds. 
The authority shall be entitled to issue bonds, bond anticipation notes, trust indentures, deed to secure obligations, security agreements and mortgages as provided under the provisions of O.C.G.A. § 36-62-8, subject to the limitations of O.C.G.A. § 36-62-9. 
(Res. of 11-10-2009, § 11) 
Sec. 2-140.8. - Dissolution. 
If for any reason the separate corporate existence of the authority is terminated and dissolved, any and all property owned by the authority shall be transferred and assigned to the host county wherein the property is located. 
(Res. of 11-10-2009, § 12) 
Sec. 2-140.9. - Amendment. 
The board, by majority vote, shall have the right to amend these articles of organization, so long as such amendment does not violate any of the provisions of the Development Authority Law for the State of Georgia, as referenced herein. 
(Res. of 11-10-2009, § 13) 
DIVISION 5. - HOSPITAL AUTHORITY 

Sec. 2-141. - Declaration of need. 
The board of commissioners declares that there is need for a hospital authority to function in the county. 
(Ord. of 1-1-1946, § a) 
Sec. 2-142. - Created; terms. 
(a)  There is created in and for the county a public body corporate and politic to be known as the hospital authority of the county, which shall consist of a board of not less than five, nor more than nine trustees, which board of trustees are authorized to exercise the powers in the county conferred under 1941 Ga. Laws, page 241 and O.C.G.A. § 31-7-72 et seq. 
(b)  The initial board of trustees shall consist of five members to serve from one year to five years, and their successors shall serve for five years. 
(Ord. of 1-1-1946, §§ b, c) 
DIVISION 6. - BOARD OF ELECTORS AND REGISTRATION 

Sec. 2-143. - Established. 
The Georgia General Assembly established a Crisp County Board of Elections and Registration, to be effective July 1, 2005, through enactment of Act. No. 182 (H.B. 415) by the General Assembly. 
(Res. of 12-14-2004) 
Sec. 2-144. - Members; appointment. 
The membership of the county board of elections and registration, shall be a chairperson and four members; the chairperson to be appointed by the board of commissioners of Crisp County, one member to be appointed by the Democratic Executive Committee, one member to be appointed by the Republican Executive Committee, and two members to be nominated by the Grand Jury of Crisp County and appointed by the Chief Superior Court Judge of the Cordele Judicial Circuit. 
(Res. of 12-14-2004) 
DIVISION 7. - BOARD OF TAX ASSESSORS 

Sec. 2-145. - Board of tax assessors term. 
The Board of Commissioners of Crisp County establish the regular terms of the Crisp County Board of Tax Assessors to be terms of four years. In order to align these terms to assure that a majority of the board of tax assessors' terms do not expire within the same year, the Board of Commissioners of Crisp County directs that two of the terms of the Crisp County Board of Tax Assessors of those appointed in 2007 be extended for one year for an initial term of five years with subsequent terms being of four years. 
(Res. of 7-10-2007) 
Secs. 2-146—2-160. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE IV. - OFFICERS AND EMPLOYEES[7] 
Footnotes: 
--- (7) --- 
Editor's note— The county compiles and publishes separately additional administrative regulations in its manual of personnel policies and procedures. The manual includes the county's drug free work place policy and retirement plan for county employees. Official copies of the referenced documentation are on file in the office of the clerk of the board of commissioners. 
Cross reference— Office of director of emergency management, § 26-33. 
State Law reference— Expenditure of county funds for insurance and employment benefits authorized, O.C.G.A. § 36-1-11.1; employment of additional temporary personnel and equipment for assistance of county officers or departments authorized, O.C.G.A. § 36-1-11; civil service system for county employees authorized, O.C.G.A. § 36-1-21(a); Fair Employment Practices Act of 1978, O.C.G.A. § 45-19-20 et seq.; municipal or county governments not to require residence as condition of employment, O.C.G.A. § 45-2-5; random drug testing of state employees in high-risk jobs, O.C.G.A. § 45-20-90 et seq.; Public Employee Hazardous Chemical Protection and Right to Know Act of 1988, O.C.G.A. § 45-22-1 et seq.; Drug-Free Public Work Force Act of 1990, O.C.G.A. § 45-23-1 et seq.; social security coverage for employees of the state and political subdivisions of the state, O.C.G.A. § 47-18-1 et seq.; Public Retirement Systems Standards Law, O.C.G.A. § 47-20-1 et seq.; authority to maintain and modify retirement or pension systems, Ga. Const. art. IX, § II, ¶ III(a)(14). 

DIVISION 1. - GENERALLY 

Sec. 2-161. - Employment status of planning department personnel. 
The ordinance enacted on October 9, 1990, which adopted various standard construction codes, is hereby, rescinded to the extent that the same grants the building official and chief building inspector employment status which may be terminated only for cause. The personnel of the county planning department shall be, and are hereby, employees subject to the provisions of the county personnel policies. 
(Ord. of 3-21-2002) 
Secs. 2-162—2-180. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 2. - COUNTY ADMINISTRATOR[8] 

Footnotes: 
--- (8) --- 
State Law reference— County manager authorized, O.C.G.A. § 36-5-22. 

Sec. 2-181. - Responsibilities. 
The responsibilities of the county administrator shall include, but not be limited to, serving as ex officio clerk to the board of commissioners, performing general administrative and supervisory work in coordinating day-to-day operation of county government, the maintenance of records and documents for the board of commissioners, serving as liaison with county departments and elected officials, interpreting and implementing policies set by the board of commissioners, assisting department heads and elected officials in the solution of technical problems on request, representing the Board of Commissioners at meetings of state and county boards and agencies as requested by the board of commissioners, conferring with department heads and preparing, together with the financial director, an annual budget for approval by the board of commissioners, preparing the agenda for the meetings of the board of commissioners, administering the county personnel policy, supervising the administration of the county retirement system and life and health insurance programs; and performing other related duties as required or directed by the board of commissioners. 
(Res. of 7-10-2002) 
Secs. 2-182—2-200. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 3. - RECREATION DEPARTMENT RETIREMENT PLAN TRANSFER[9] 

Footnotes: 
--- (9) --- 
State Law reference— State parks, O.C.G.A. § 12-3-1 et seq.; establishment of recreation systems, O.C.G.A. § 36-64-1 et seq.; recreation boards, O.C.G.A. § 36-64-5; Georgia state games commission, O.C.G.A. § 50-12-40 et seq.; authority to provide parks, recreation areas, programs and facilities, Ga. Const. art. IX, § II, ¶ III(a)(5). 

Sec. 2-201. - Termination of participation in the Georgia Municipal Employees Benefit System. 
The recreation department's participation in the Georgia Municipal Employees Benefit System is terminated effective as of the close of business Friday, June 30, 2000. The agreement providing for the recreation department's participation in the Georgia Municipal Employees Benefit System, the trust agreement between the recreation department and the Georgia Municipal Employees Benefit System, and the Georgia Municipal Employees Benefit System-administered recreation department retirement plan shall be considered terminated effective as of such date. 
(Ord. of 6-16-2000, § 1) 
Sec. 2-202. - Designation of successor trustees. 
The Board of Trustees of the Association of County Commissioners of Georgia (ACCG) Defined Benefit Plan is designated to serve as successor trustees to the Georgia Municipal Employees Benefit System board of trustees and is authorized and directed to receive assets to be transferred to it from the recreation department trust fund held by Georgia Municipal Employees Benefit System. 
(Ord. of 6-16-2000, § 2) 
Sec. 2-203. - Transfer of balance. 
(a)  The board of trustees of Georgia Municipal Employees Benefit System is authorized and directed to transfer the balance of any and all assets in the recreation department trust fund held by Georgia Municipal Employees Benefit System on and as of June 30, 2000, to the Board of Trustees of the Association of County Commissioners of Georgia (ACCG) Defined Benefit Plan as successor trustees. Trust fund earnings for the month of June 2000, shall be calculated and applied by multiplying the balance in the account as of June 30, 2000, by 1/12 of eight percent. Any earnings or losses which would have otherwise been credited to or debited from the trust fund after June 30, 2000, shall not be taken into account. Georgia Municipal Employees Benefit System is authorized to deduct from the trust fund balance an appropriate fee for administrative services provided in effecting the termination of the recreation department's participation in Georgia Municipal Employees Benefit System and the transfer of assets. 
(b)  Within a reasonable time prior to the transfer of assets as stated in subsection (a) of this section, the county shall provide to Georgia Municipal Employees Benefit System information necessary to calculate the accrued benefits of participants under the Georgia Municipal Employees Benefit System-administered recreation department retirement plan as of June 30, 2000. Upon receipt of such information and prior to the transfer of assets, Georgia Municipal Employees Benefit System is authorized and directed to prepare and submit to the Pension Service Company, the administrator of the Association of County Commissioners of Georgia (ACCG) Defined Benefit Plan, a list of all such participants, showing for each the present value of his accrued benefit, determined based upon the information provided by the county and in accordance with actuarial assumptions contained in article VIII, section 7 of the Georgia Municipal Employees Benefit System-administered recreation department plan. 
(Ord. of 6-16-2000, §§ 3, 4) 
Sec. 2-204. - Retirement rights of employees, participants and beneficiaries. 
The county shall ensure that the retirement rights of employees, participants and beneficiaries accrued as of June 30, 2000, under the Georgia Municipal Employees Benefit System-administered recreation department retirement plan shall not be impaired by virtue of the transfer of recreation department employees to the county, or by their transfer to the Association of County Commissioners of Georgia (ACCG) Defined Benefit Plan. 
(Ord. of 6-16-2000, § 5) 
Sec. 2-205. - No further responsibility or obligation after transfer of assets. 
Upon the transfer of assets to the Board of Trustees of the Association of County Commissioners of Georgia (ACCG) Defined Benefit Plan, the City of Cordele, Georgia Municipal Employees Benefit System and the Georgia Municipal Association (GMA) shall have no further responsibility or obligation to provide or administer retirement or other benefits for employees or retirees of the recreation department or their beneficiaries. The Georgia Municipal Employees Benefit System Board of Trustees' responsibility for the investment of assets held on behalf of the Georgia Municipal Employees Benefit System-administered recreation department retirement plan trust fund shall also cease upon such transfer. Georgia Municipal Employees Benefit System, the Georgia Municipal Association and their officers and employees are specifically held harmless by the county from any liability, claims or suits arising from the transfer of recreation department employees to the county, or their transfer to the Association of County Commissioners of Georgia (ACCG) Defined Benefit Plan. Georgia Municipal Employees Benefit System and Georgia Municipal Association shall be responsible only for the proper accounting and transfer of assets held in the recreation department retirement plan trust fund in accordance with this article. 
(Ord. of 6-16-2000, § 6) 
Secs. 2-206—2-220. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE V. - FINANCE[10] 
Footnotes: 
--- (10) --- 
Editor's note— The county has adopted policies and procedures, revised in 1993, relating to the Crisp County Revolving Loan Fund. Official copies of the policies and procedures are on file in the office of the clerk of the board of commissioners. 
Cross reference— Any ordinance or resolution promising or guaranteeing the payment of money for the county or authorizing the issuance of any bonds of the county or any evidence of the county's indebtedness saved from repeal, § 1-6(2); taxation, ch. 58.

DIVISION 1. - GENERALLY 

Sec. 2-221. - Fiscal year. 
The fiscal year for the county shall commence on July 1 and conclude on June 30. 
State Law reference— Establishment of fiscal year required, O.C.G.A. § 36-81-3(a).
