DIVISION 2. - UNIFORM CHART OF ACCOUNTS 

Sec. 2-241. - Findings. 
O.C.G.A. § 36-81-3(e) requires the state department of community affairs, in cooperation with the Association of County Commissioners of Georgia and Georgia Municipal Association to develop local government uniform charts of accounts. O.C.G.A. § 36-81-3(e) further requires the state auditor approval prior to the adoption of uniform charts of accounts by the state department of community affairs. O.C.G.A. § 36-81-3(e) further requires all units of local government in the state to adopt the initial uniform chart of accounts adopted by the state department of community affairs. The state department of community affairs has adopted an initial uniform charts of accounts. 
Sec. 2-242. - Adopted. 
The initial uniform chart of accounts, adopted by the state department of community affairs, is adopted and shall be used by all departments and agencies of the county for all budgetary and accounting purposes effective on or after July 1, 2001, including without limitation, all accounting records, audited financial statements, including comprehensive annual financial reports, and reports to state agencies. 
(Res. of 8-14-2001) 
Chapter 6 - ALCOHOLIC BEVERAGES[1] 
Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
Cross reference— Businesses, ch. 22. 
State Law reference— Georgia Alcoholic Beverage Code, O.C.G.A. § 3-1-1 et seq. 

ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 

Sec. 6-1. - Definitions. 
The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this chapter, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
Alcohol means ethyl alcohol, hydrated oxide of ethyl, or spirits of wine, from whatever source or by whatever process produced. 
Alcoholic beverage means and includes all alcohol, distilled spirits, beer, malt beverage, wine or fortified wine. 
Club means any religious, charitable or fraternal organization holding a current national charter and shall not include locally chartered corporations or local organizations operating under a registered or unregistered name. 
Distilled spirits means any alcoholic beverage obtained by distillation or containing more than 21 percent alcohol by volume, including, but not limited to, all fortified wines. 
Fortified wine means any alcoholic beverage containing more than 21 percent alcohol by volume made from fruits, berries or grapes either by natural fermentation or by natural fermentation with brandy added. The term includes, but is not limited to, brandy. 
Malt beverage means any alcoholic beverage obtained by the fermentation of any infusion or decoction of barley, malt, hops, or any other similar product, or any combination of such products in water, containing not more than six percent alcohol by volume and including ale, porter, brown, stout, lager beer, small beer and strong beer. The term does not include sake, known as Japanese rice wine. 
Package means a bottle, can, keg, barrel or other original consumer container. 
Restaurant means an establishment maintained, advertised and held out to the public as a place where meals are actually and regularly served, being provided with an adequate and sanitary kitchen conforming to applicable laws and regulations, with dining room equipment and personnel to serve complete meals, and which serves at least one complete meal per day at least six days per week (with the exception of holidays, vacations and periods of redecorating), food service being the principal business conducted with the sale of wine and malt beverages being only incidental thereto. 
Retail consumption dealer means any person who sells alcoholic beverages for consumption on the premises at retail only to consumers and not for resale. 
Retail distilled spirits dealer means any person who sells distilled spirits in unbroken packages at retail only to consumers and not for resale. 
Retail malt beverages dealer means any person who engages in selling malt beverages at retail within the county and shall include any person serving malt beverages for a pecuniary consideration within the county. 
Wholesale malt beverages dealer means any person who sells malt beverages to a retail malt beverages dealer. 
Wine means any alcoholic beverage containing not more than 21 percent alcohol by volume made from fruits, berries or grapes either by natural fermentation or by natural fermentation with brandy added. The term "wine" includes, but is not limited to, all sparkling wines, champagnes, combinations of such beverages, vermouths, special natural wines, rectified wines and like products. The terms does not include cooking wine mixed with salt or other ingredients so as to render it unfit for human consumption as a beverage. A liquid shall first be deemed to be a wine at that point in the manufacturing process when it conforms to this definition. 
(Res. of 5-12-1992, art. I, § 1.01) 
Cross reference— Definitions generally, § 1-2. 
Sec. 6-2. - Violations. 
Violations of this chapter shall be punished upon conviction in the magistrate court of the county as provided in section 1-11. 
(Res. of 5-12-1992, art. I, § 1.08) 
Sec. 6-3. - Sale on election days. 
Alcoholic beverages which are licensed for sale in the county may be sold on all election days during normal business hours established by this chapter and regulation of sales of alcoholic beverages by ordinance. 
(Res. of 5-12-1992, art. I, § 1.02) 
Sec. 6-4. - Possession on county property or public places. 
(a)  Drinking. It shall be unlawful for any person to drink any alcoholic beverage upon property of the county or upon any open premises adjacent to any public business in the county, whether or not such person is located in a vehicle. 
(b)  Containers. It shall be unlawful for any person to have in his hand, or upon his person, or in any vehicle, any open container used, or which has been used, for alcoholic beverages, upon the property of the county or upon any open premises adjacent to any public business in the county. 
(Res. of 5-12-1992, art. I, §§ 1.03, 1.04) 
Sec. 6-5. - Hours of sale. 
(a)  Prescribed. It shall be unlawful for any person holding a retail consumption dealer license in the county, or for any unlicensed person, to offer for sale at retail, or to give away in or upon any such licensee's premises, or the premises of an unlicensed person, any alcoholic beverages between the hours of 1:30 a.m. and 7:00 a.m. of any Monday, Tuesday, Wednesday, Thursday or Friday, or between the hours of 12:00 midnight Saturday and 12:30 p.m. Sunday or between the hours of 12:00 midnight Sunday and 7:00 a.m. Monday. 
(b)  Patron on premises during closing hours. 
(1)  It shall be unlawful for any retail consumption dealer, including, but not limited to, restaurants and clubs, to keep open for business or admit the public to, or permit the public to remain within, or permit the consumption of alcoholic beverages in or upon the premises in which alcoholic beverages are sold at retail for a period of longer than 30 minutes after the hours within which the sale of alcoholic beverages are prohibited, during which 30 minutes customers will be permitted to consume alcoholic beverages which were purchased during legal hours of sale. 
(2)  Food service establishments also holding a retail consumption license may reopen for business between the hours of 6:00 a.m. and 12:30 p.m. Sunday, during which time retail customers may be provided service and products not prohibited by section 6-6. It shall be unlawful for any licensee to admit the public to, or permit the public to remain within, the licensee's premises on Sunday at any times other than between the hours of 6:00 a.m. and 12:00 midnight. 
(Res. of 5-12-1992, art. I, §§ 1.05, 1.06; Ord. of 11-12-2014(2)) 
Sec. 6-6. - Sale of other commodities; drinking on premises prohibited. 
No licensed retailer may sell or offer for sale or display or keep in stock at his place of business where distilled spirits, wine and malt beverages are offered for sale any other product or commodity except packaged ice and beverages containing no alcohol which are commonly used to dilute distilled spirits and wine, and the sale of such excepted beverages and ice may be conducted only upon payment of the appropriate occupation tax. Drinking any beverages containing alcohol upon the retailer's premises is prohibited. 
(Res. of 5-12-1992, art. I, § 1.07) 
Sec. 6-7. - Suspension or revocation of license for violation. 
(a)  In addition to all other fines and penalties provided by this chapter or by applicable state law, the board of commissioners may suspend or revoke for cause appearing sufficient to the commission the alcoholic beverage license of any person in the county, including, but not limited to, cause arising for violation of the provisions of this chapter and/or conviction of such violation in the county magistrate court. 
(b)  Upon written notice delivered to a licensee under this chapter signed by the county administrator, the sheriff or the chairman of the board of commissioners recommending that the license of such licensee should be revoked under the provisions of this section, the board of commissioners may conduct a hearing at a regular or special meeting wherein evidence shall be heard and the board of commissioners by majority vote may suspend or revoke such alcoholic beverage license. The notice shall state the time and place of hearing and a copy thereof shall be filed in the permanent records of the board of commissioners by delivery to the county administrator. 
(c)  A licensee under this chapter to whom notice is given must appear at such hearing or his absence shall be considered a waiver of his right to appear and a consent to the action taken by the board of commissioners. Such licensee may be represented by an attorney and shall be allowed to present evidence. 
(d)  Appeal from the decision of the board of commissioners under this section shall be governed by the laws of the state. 
(Res. of 5-12-1992, art. I, § 1.08) 
Secs. 6-8—6-40. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE II. - MALT BEVERAGES 

Sec. 6-41. - License required for malt beverage dealers. 
There is levied, assessed and required an annual license for any person to engage in the sale of malt beverages in the county. It shall be unlawful for any person to engage in the sale of malt beverages in the county without first registering and paying the license fee, which shall be $75.00 per calendar year or any part thereof. 
(Res. of 5-12-1992, art. II, § 2.01) 
Sec. 6-42. - Tax levied. 
There is imposed and levied a specific excise tax upon all malt beverages dealers within the county as follows: 
(1)  Per 12 ounces or fractional part thereof, regardless of container, $0.05. 
(2)  Per container of 15½ gallons, or fractional part thereof, of tap or draft malt beverages, $6.00. 
(Res. of 5-12-1992, art. II, § 2.02) 
Sec. 6-43. - Possession of specified number of bottles, presumption of business. 
Any person having located in his place of business more than 24 bottles of malt beverages at any one time shall be presumed to be in the business of selling malt beverages for a pecuniary consideration. 
(Res. of 5-12-1992, art. II, § 2.03) 
Sec. 6-44. - Additional to other taxes and licenses; payment and collection procedure. 
The taxes imposed and levied by section 6-42 shall be in addition to all other taxes or licenses or license fees levied or imposed upon malt beverage dealers, and it may be added by the retail malt beverages dealer to the retail price and collected from each customer. 
(Res. of 5-12-1992, art. II, § 2.04) 
Secs. 6-45—6-80. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE III. - WINE 

Sec. 6-81. - Sale in package store only; exception; license for food service establishments. 
Retail sales of wine shall be made in the county at retail package stores duly licensed by the county for the sale of distilled spirits, provided that a separate retail license for the sale of wine in the county may be purchased from the county by a restaurant, hotel, motel or other business engaged in selling food to the public for consumption upon the premises where sold, when each of the following conditions are complied with: 
(1)  Application for a separate retail wine license for the sale of wine shall be made in writing to the board of commissioners, setting forth the same information required for application for a retail license for the sale of distilled spirits. Any application for a separate retail wine license under this section acknowledges by such application that such license is a privilege and not a right. 
(2)  The fee for a separate retail wine license shall be $500.00 per year and shall be renewable on the anniversary date of the initial application, which amount shall accompany the application, provided, however, that renewals of such license shall not require formal application, but shall be as provided by sections of this chapter regulating the sale of distilled spirits, as the same provides for renewals of licenses. 
(3)  An establishment licensed under a separate retail wine license shall be subject to the same tax per case of wine purchased as is provided by section 6-82. 
(4)  An establishment licensed under a separate retail wine license is expressly authorized to sell wine by the bottle and/or by the glass to retail customers upon the premises to be consumed with food, and any other sale of wine under this article, other than with food, is expressly prohibited. 
(Res. of 5-12-1992, art. III, § 3.01) 
Sec. 6-82. - Tax on cases purchased by retail package store. 
Any duly licensed retail package store in the county shall also have the right and privilege to sell wine without any additional license fee, except that there shall be a specific tax in the amount of $2.40 on each case of wine purchased by a retail package store. 
(Res. of 5-12-1992, art. III, § 3.02) 
Sec. 6-83. - License required for wholesaler. 
There is levied, assessed and required a license fee in an amount as determined by the board of commissioners from time to time and listed in the schedule of fees and charges maintained in the county administrator's office for any person to engage in the wholesale sale of wine in the county. 
(Res. of 5-12-1992, art. III, § 3.03) 
Sec. 6-84. - Retailers subject to laws, regulations governing sale of spirits. 
All retail sales of wine shall be subject to the ordinances, rules and regulations of the county applicable to the retail sale of distilled spirits. 
(Res. of 5-12-1992, art. III, § 3.04) 
Secs. 6-85—6-110. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE IV. - DISTILLED SPIRITS 
DIVISION 1. - GENERALLY 

Sec. 6-111. - Excise tax. 
There is levied on all sales of distilled spirits, excluding fortified wine, an excise tax of $0.22 per liter. This tax is in addition to all other licenses or taxes imposed by the county. 
(Res. of 5-12-1992, art. IV, § 4.04) 
Sec. 6-112. - Wholesaler's invoices. 
Any wholesale dealer who sells to retail package stores in the county shall file a copy of each invoice with the county administrator. This invoice shall be identical to the one furnished to the United States Internal Revenue Service. 
(Res. of 5-12-1992, art. IV, § 4.06) 
Sec. 6-113. - Additional remedy in default in payment of sums due. 
In the event of default in the payment of any amount due under the provisions of this article on the part of any person, the collection of the same shall, in addition to other penalties, be enforced and executed as for county taxes. 
(Res. of 5-12-1992, art. IV, § 4.07) 
Sec. 6-114. - Stock to be kept on premises; only one entrance permitted; premises to be open to view. 
All distilled spirits possessed by a licensee under this article shall be kept in the package store. No retailer's place of business shall have more than one entrance which must open on a public street and such place of business shall have no other entrance and shall contain no vestibule, closet, booth or other place where persons may conceal themselves to consume alcoholic beverages. 
(Res. of 5-12-1992, art. IV, § 4.14) 
Sec. 6-115. - Access to other establishments prohibited; windows to face on same street as entrance. 
No package store shall be operated in conjunction with or open into or have access to or from any restaurant, lunchroom, dining room, dancehall or other store or business of any kind or character. The windows in every package store shall face the same public street faced by the entrance to the package store and such windows shall not be obstructed or obscured in any manner, except as provided in section 6-116. 
(Res. of 5-12-1992, art. IV, § 4.15) 
Sec. 6-116. - Obstructing windows. 
No place of business operating under this article shall display on the exterior thereof any neon or fluorescent signs to advertise either the name or the products of the store. Any interior sign shall be confined to the upper part of the window so as not to obstruct the view of the interior of the package store. 
(Res. of 5-12-1992, art. IV, § 4.16) 
Sec. 6-117. - Persons under 21 years of age prohibited on premises. 
No person under 21 years of age shall be permitted to enter a retail package store, and each licensee under this article shall be held strictly responsible for the enforcement of this section. 
(Res. of 5-12-1992, art. IV, § 4.17) 
Secs. 6-118—6-140. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 2. - LICENSE 

Sec. 6-141. - Required. 
There is levied, assessed and required an annual license for any person to engage in the sale of distilled spirits in the county. It shall be unlawful for any person to engage in the sale of distilled spirits without first registering and paying such license fee; which license fee shall be in the amount of $4,000.00 per calendar year, payable $2,000.00 on January 1 of each year and $2,000.00 on July 1 of each year. 
(Res. of 5-12-1992, art. IV, § 4.01) 
Sec. 6-142. - Application—Contents. 
(a)  The person desiring a license under this division shall first make written application under oath to the board of commissioners setting forth the following information: 
(1)  The name of the applicant, and if a firm the names of all the members thereof, and if a corporation the names of all the directors, officers and stockholders thereof. 
(2)  Whether any other person is to be interested directly or indirectly in the proposed business and if the interested party is a person, the name of such person, and if the interested party is a firm, the names of all the members thereof, and if the interested party is a corporation, the names of all the directors, officers and stockholders thereof. 
(3)  The location of the proposed business giving the name of the street and the street number. 
(4)  The length of residence in the county of the applicant or the persons listed in subsection (a)(2) of this section. 
(5)  Any additional information that the board of commissioners may request of the person applying for the license. 
(b)  The making of any untrue or misleading statement in the application for a license under this division shall be sufficient cause for the denial, suspension, revocation or cancellation of such license by the board of commissioners without refund of any part of the license fee. 
(c)  Application for renewal of a license issued under this division shall be executed in the same manner as the application for the original license. 
(Res. of 5-12-1992, art. IV, § 4.02) 
Sec. 6-143. - Same—Forms; submitting fee; refund. 
All applications and notices provided for in this division shall be made on forms provided by the county. Application for a license shall be accompanied either in lawful money of the United States, certified check or cashiers check payable to the county for the proper amount of the license fee. If the applicant is refused a license by the revenue commissioner of the state, the license fee shall be returned to the applicant. The provisions of this section do not apply to suspension or revocation of a license by the board of commissioners or by the revenue commissioner of the state, or by any agency of the United States of America or by any court. 
(Res. of 5-12-1992, art. IV, § 4.03) 
Sec. 6-144. - License period; credit for fee on partial year; no proration; transferability. 
(a)  The license or privilege to sell distilled spirits shall be issued or granted for a period no longer than 12 months. The license shall expire on December 31 of the year in which it is granted. However, any person having paid the full year's license fee shall be entitled to a credit on the next year's license in an amount representing the unused portion of the license for the initial year of purchase. In calculating the unused portion of such license, credit shall be allowed by quarters so that any person commencing business between January 1 and April 1 shall not be allowed any credit on the next year's license. Any person commencing business after April 1 and before July 1 shall be allowed credit on the next year's license for one quarter. Any person commencing business on or after July 1 and before October 1 shall be allowed credit on the next year's license for one-half. Any person commencing business on or after October 1 and before December 1 shall be allowed credit of three-fourths on the next year's license. The credit so calculated shall not be transferable or payable except in a license granted for the next succeeding year, and in order to get credit for the unused portion of the license the person must apply and pay for the license before February 1 of the next succeeding year. 
(b)  No license to sell distilled spirits shall be prorated for any part of the year. 
(c)  No license to sell distilled spirits shall be transferable from one licensee to another person. 
(Res. of 5-12-1992, art. IV, § 4.05) 
Sec. 6-145. - Payment of delinquent sums due county prerequisite to issuance of license. 
In addition to the licenses imposed under this division, there is further imposed as a condition precedent to the issuance of any license under this division, the payment of all past due licenses, ad valorem taxes and other taxes due to the county. 
(Res. of 5-12-1992, art. IV, § 4.08) 
Sec. 6-146. - Private club license. 
Upon the payment of a fee as determined by the board of commissioners from time to time and listed in the schedule of fees and charges maintained in the county administrator's office, any club, patriotic organization, charitable organization or fraternal organization which has been in operation in the county for a continuous period of five years immediately prior to application for a license under this division, under a national charter, and which is nonprofit in that the individual members do not receive any dividends or share in the profits shall be licensed to make retail sales provided retail sales shall be made on the premises at its principal location to its members only. 
(Res. of 5-12-1992, art. IV, § 4.09) 
Sec. 6-147. - Other laws and regulations applicable; revocation of license for violation. 
Every licensee under this division shall strictly comply with the laws and regulations of the United States of America, the state and the state revenue commission which regulate and control distilled spirits. In the event that any licensee is convicted of violating any federal or state law relating to the sale of alcoholic beverages, such license is automatically revoked and no part of the license money shall be refunded. 
(Res. of 5-12-1992, art. IV, § 4.10) 
Sec. 6-148. - Change of licensee's location. 
The location named in a licensee's application under this division shall not be changed without permission of and approval of the board of commissioners. 
(Res. of 5-12-1992, art. IV, § 4.11) 
Sec. 6-149. - Sale declared privilege, not right; privilege denied to convicted felon. 
No person who has been convicted of a felony under federal laws or the laws of any state shall be granted a license to sell distilled spirits. 
(Res. of 5-12-1992, art. IV, § 4.12) 
Sec. 6-150. - Zoning requirements; exceptions. 
No license for the sale of spirituous liquors or distilled spirits shall be granted for a business location in any district designated as R-1 residential, R-2 residential, R-12, R-7.5S, R-7.5, R-4, E-I, PEH, PW or M-1 industrial under the zoning ordinance. Private clubs, patriotic organizations or fraternal organizations meeting all of the requirements of section 6-146 are excepted if in compliance with such zoning regulations. 
(Res. of 5-12-1992, art. IV, § 4.13) 
Secs. 6-151—6-169. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE V. - LIQUOR BY THE DRINK 
DIVISION 1. - GENERALLY 

Sec. 6-170. - Purposes. 
(a)  The purposes of this chapter shall include, without necessarily being limited to, the following: 
(1)  Compliance with and effectuation of the general state law. 
(2)  Prevention and control of the sale of alcoholic beverages by certain persons; 
(3)  Ensuring that any licenses issued for the consumption of alcoholic beverages on the premises are issued only to a legitimate restaurant or private club as defined in this chapter. 
(4)  The protection of schools, homes, churches, parks, and other institutions. 
(5)  Protection of the public health, safety, and welfare. 
(b)  To the maximum extent permissible under state and federal law, the business of selling alcoholic beverages shall under this chapter be considered to be a privilege to be accorded in conformity with the foregoing and other public policies of the county, rather than a right. 
(Ord. of 11-14-2006) 
Sec. 6-171. - Definitions. 
(a)  Unless a contrary intention is clearly apparent from the context, the following terms used in this chapter shall have the following meaning: 
Alcoholic beverage means and includes all alcohol, malt beverages, distilled spirits, wine and fortified wines defined in this section. 
County means the Crisp County and when used in a geographical sense means the territorial limits of the unincorporated portion of Crisp County. 
County Administrator means the county administrator of Crisp County. 
Distilled spirits means any alcoholic beverage obtained by distillation or containing more than 21 percent alcohol by volume, including, but not limited to, all fortified wines. 
Interest includes any pecuniary interest and any ownership interest, whether present or future, whole or partial, legal or beneficial, contingent or vested, direct or indirect, and any right, power, or authority of control. 
Licensed premises includes not only the room wherein alcoholic beverages are sold or served but also the entire building in which such room is located, except that when such a room is located in a hotel, motel, or similar facility or in a shopping center only such room and any adjoining storage, office, toilet, and other similar rooms shall constitute the "licensed premises." 
Licensee includes an individual licensee and in the case of a partnership or corporation includes both the partnership or corporation and the named licensee. 
Majority stockholder means the person, if any, who owns more than 50 percent of the voting stock of a corporation; if no person owns more than 50 percent of the voting [stock] of a corporation, the "majority stockholder" is the person owning more of the voting stock than any other person; and if two or more persons each own the same amount of the voting stock of a corporation and each own more of the voting stock than any other person, then any one of such persons may act as the "majority stockholder." 
County commission means the board of commissioners of Crisp County. 
Mixed drink or liquor by the drink means any distilled spirits served for consumption on the premises, whether or not diluted by water or any other substance. 
Named licensee means the person acting as such for a partnership or corporation pursuant to this section. 
Person includes a corporation, partnership, association, club or institution. 
Semipublic parking facility means any privately owned area wherein motor vehicles may be parked by the public in conjunction with any business, enterprise, commercial establishment, office building, church, school, or multiple-family residential building. 
(b)  Unless a contrary intention is clearly apparent from the context, any term used in this chapter shall have the same meaning as when used in comparable provision of the Georgia Alcoholic Beverage Code, O.C.G.A. title 3. 
(c)  As used in this chapter, the singular and plural shall each include the other, the masculine and feminine shall each include the other, and any verb tense may include any other verb tense. 
(d)  As used in this chapter, the term "may" is permissive and the term "shall" is mandatory. 
(Ord. of 11-14-2006) 
Sec. 6-172. - Violations; penalty. 
(a)  Any person who violates any provision of this chapter shall, upon conviction in the court of appropriate jurisdiction, be punished as provided in this Code, which may include a fine. Any such punishment, if imposed, shall be in addition to and not in lieu of any license suspension or revocation under this chapter. 
(b)  The violation of any of the provisions of this chapter, including the maximum occupant load, shall be grounds for fines, suspension, or revocation of any license issued hereunder. 
(1)  For the first violation there shall be a $1,000.00 fine. 
(2)  For the second violation, the date of occurrence of which is within any 60-month period of the first violation, there shall be a $1,000.00 fine and a 30-day suspension of the license privileges. 
(3)  For any third violation, the date of occurrence of which is within any 60-month period of the first violation, there shall be a $1,000.00 fine and a revocation of the license privileges by the Board of Commissioners of Crisp County. 
(4)  Any suspension, or revocation of a license shall first require notice to the license holder of a due process hearing before the Board of Commissioners of Crisp County, as required by section 6-199 herein. 
(5)  A license holder who receives a suspension or revocation of his license may not be an officer, director or shareholder of any succeeding entity that holds a license from the county during his period of suspension. 
(Ord. of 11-14-2006) 
Sec. 6-173. - County administrator's duties. 
The county administrator, or the county administrator's designee, is hereby vested with the following duties and powers: 
(a)  To take all applications, to screen, verify, investigate and review all initial applications for licenses for the sale of liquor by the drink. 
(b)  To recommend to the county commission modifications to the ordinances and policies of the county pertaining to the regulation control and taxing of liquor by the drink. 
(c)  To hear complaints, suggestions and recommendations from the sheriff's department, state officials, alcoholic beverage providers, and the public at large as to the operation of liquor-by-the-drink outlets within the county. 
(d)  After screening, investigating and complying with all parts of this chapter, the county administrator or the county administrator's designee, with the approval of the county commission, shall grant the applicant's desired license or shall deny said license, applying all requirements of this article. 
(e)  An applicant, or any county or state official objecting to the request of the applicant, who is dissatisfied with the decision, may appeal the aggrieved action to the county commission, whose decision on the appeal shall be final. Any appeal from the decision must be filed within 30 days, and the chairman of the county commission will schedule the appeal for a hearing within 30 days. 
(f)  All renewal decisions shall be made by the county administrator with the approval county commission employing the rules and regulations of this chapter. 
(Ord. of 11-14-2006) 
Sec. 6-174—6-190. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 2. - LICENSING 

Sec. 6-191. - Required classifications, etc. 
(a)  Required. It shall be unlawful for any person to sell or offer for sale any liquor by the drink within the county except under a valid license issued under this article and in compliance with the provisions of this article. 
(b)  Pay schedule. License fees shall be payable in advance for an entire year beginning January 1 and ending December 31 of each year. If an initial fee is paid on or before June 30 of the year of application, the license fees shall not be prorated for a part of year. If an initial fee is paid after June 30 of the year of application, the license fee shall be reduced to 50 percent. The suspension or revocation of any license granted pursuant to this article shall not entitle the licensee to a return of any portion of the license fee. 
(c)  Classification fee. Class of license issued under this article, activities permitted and regulated hereunder, and the annual license fee shall be as follows: 
Liquor-by-the-drink license (for consumption on the premises) ..... $2,500.00 
(d)  Application fees. Each application for a license under this chapter shall be accompanied by a nonrefundable application fee in the amount of $650.00. 
(e)  Payment of fees. Application fees shall be paid at the time the application is filed and shall not be refunded under any circumstances. An applicant may pay the annual license fee at the time the application is filed; and in such event the annual license fee shall be refunded if the license applied for is not issued. If the annual license fee is not paid at the time of the application, the annual license fee shall be paid prior to the issuance of the license by the county administrator, and no later than 90 days after notification of approval. Failure to pay within 90 days shall render the application void and a new application must be submitted including a new $650.00 application fee. 
(Ord. of 11-14-2006) 
Sec. 6-192. - Procedure for issuance. 
(a)  A license issued to an individual shall be issued in the name of the individual. A license issued to a partnership shall be issued in the name of the partnership and in the name of one of the partners who shall be the named licensee. A license issued to a corporation having as its business the sale of liquor by the drink shall be issued in the name of the corporation and in the name of the majority stockholder or a principal officer of the corporation; and such majority stockholder or officer shall be the named licensee. A license issued to a corporation having as its business an activity other than the sale of liquor by the drink shall be issued in the name of the corporation and in the name of the officer or employee of the corporation primarily responsible for the operation of the licensed premises; and such officer or employee shall be the named licensee. 
(b)  In the case of a partnership, each partner shall join as an applicant for the license and each partner must meet the qualifications of an individual licensee, as provided herein. 
(c)  In the case of a corporation having as its business the sale of liquor by the drink, the majority stockholder and each principal officer of the corporation shall join as applicants for the license; and each such person must meet the qualifications of an individual licensee. 
(d)  In the case of a corporation having as its principal business an activity other than the sale of liquor by the drink, the officer or employee who is to be the named licensee shall be the applicant and must meet the qualifications of an individual licensee, as provided herein; provided, however, that the county administrator, with the approval of the county commission, may require the fingerprinting and investigation of officers and shareholders of the corporation if they deem it necessary in making their investigation. 
(e)  In the case of a partnership, each partner shall be responsible for the actions of the named licensee and the conduct of the licensed business. In the case of a corporation, the corporation shall be responsible for the actions of the named licensee and the conduct of the licensed business. 
(Ord. of 11-14-2006) 
Sec. 6-193. - Qualifications. 
(a)  A licensee must be at least 21 years of age and a citizen of the United States of America. 
(b)  A licensee shall not have been convicted within the past five years of any felony or, misdemeanor, or violation of county alcohol ordinances within the past two years, or at any time of any criminal offense relating to alcoholic beverages, drugs, taxes or gambling. This subsection shall apply with respect to the laws of this state, other states, the United States, and other countries. A plea of nolo contendere or the forfeiture of a bond shall be considered a conviction for purposes of this subsection. The county commission may at its discretion waive the conviction of a misdemeanor for a nonalcoholic offense for purposes of this subsection if the county commission determines that the misdemeanor does not have a bearing on the applicant's fitness for a license. 
(c)  A licensee shall not have been denied a license or had a license revoked, within the five years next preceding the application, any license to sell alcoholic beverages issued by any governmental entity. 
(d)  No license for the sale of alcoholic beverages by the drink for consumption on the premises shall be issued to any applicant who does not meet the requirements of a restaurant or a private club as defined in sections 6-230 and 6-231. 
(Ord. of 11-14-2006) 
Sec. 6-194. - Application procedures. 
(a)  Application for a license for the sale of liquor by the drink in the county shall be filed with the county administrator upon forms prescribed by the county administrator (Form LD-2) and made available at the county courthouse. The application shall be subscribed by the applicant under oath and fully completed and executed. 
(b)  There shall be attached to the application a bank money order, certified check or like remittance of the application. 
(c)  As a prerequisite to the issuance of the license, the applicant shall furnish, to the sheriff of Crisp County, a complete set of fingerprints to be forwarded to the Georgia Bureau of Investigation, which shall search the files to determine past criminal activity. 
(d)  Failure to fully complete and execute an application for a license or to furnish accurately all data, information and records required by the application form as well as failure to accompany the application with the payment of the prescribed fee shall be deemed just cause for denying the application with prejudice. 
(e)  Upon proper completion of the application and payment of fees, the county administrator shall refer the application to the sheriff of Crisp County. Thereafter, the sheriff of Crisp County shall present his findings and recommendations to the county commission on the "Report of Findings and Recommendation—Sheriff's Office (Form LD-2A)." 
(f)  As a prerequisite to the issuance of a license, all businesses where liquor by the drink is consumed on the premises shall satisfy all requirements of a fire and life safety inspection performed by the county fire official and county building inspector. The prescribed inspection form shall be provided by the county fire official. In addition, all businesses where liquor by the drink is consumed on the premises, and the occupancy load is 100 or more, shall provide the county administrator with a signed fire safety report and certificate of occupancy from the state fire marshal's office. The local fire official may cause to be inspected any building or portion of any building licensed under this ordinance. 
(g)  Upon full compliance with the requirements of the fire and life safety inspections, the county fire official and building inspector shall jointly notify the county administrator for further processing of the license application. This notification shall be made using the verification form, "Fire—Life Safety—Occupancy Load Form (LD-2B)." The administrator shall sign the form and maintain it as part of the official record for the license. 
(h)  After all areas of the investigation have been completed, the county administrator will place the liquor-by-the-drink license application on the county commissioners' meeting agenda for consideration by the board of commissioners. 
(1)  If the board of commissioners approves the license application, it will be so recorded in the minutes of the meeting, the decision will be recorded on the "Application Decision Form (LD-2E)" and maintained as part of the official record for the license and the county administrator will issue the liquor-by-the-drink license to the applicant. 
(2)  If the board of commissioners denies the license application, it will be so recorded in the minutes of the meeting, the decision will be recorded on the "Application Decision Form (LD-2E)" and maintained as part of the official record for the license. The license application fee shall not be refunded. 
(Ord. of 11-14-2006) 
Sec. 6-195. - Renewal. 
All liquor-by-the-drink licensees shall be required to apply for renewal of their licenses annually on forms prescribed by the county administrator and must comply with all provisions of this article, with the exception that publication of notice, fingerprinting and background checks, as required shall not be required for renewal of a license unless there has been a change of ownership of the business or other interests therein. On renewal, the applicant shall be administered and take the oath specifically contained on the application form. The county administrator may within their discretion require fingerprinting and a full background check on any renewal at any time. 
(Ord. of 11-14-2006) 
Sec. 6-196. - Transfer. 
(a)  Except as provided in this section, no license shall be transferable to any other person or location. 
(b)  If a licensee seeks to move his place of business from the licensee's premises to another place within the county, application shall be made as for an original license. 
(c)  In the case of death of an owner of a license or financial interest therein, such license or interest therein may be transferred to the administrator, executor, or adult heir or heirs of the deceased unless the county administrator, with the approval of the county commission, determines that it would otherwise violate this chapter. If the transferee cannot meet all the requirements of this chapter within 30 days, the license shall be revoked. 
(d)  Nothing in this section shall prohibit one or more partners in a partnership from retiring therefrom in favor of one or more of the other partners; provided such withdrawal shall not, without application for an issuance of a new license, introduce any new partner or result in any new person acquiring an interest in the licensed business. 
(e)  Where a license is issued to a corporation having as its principal business an activity other than the sale of liquor by the drink, a change in the named licensee may be permitted by the county administrator, with the approval of the county commission, if the new named licensee meets the requirements of new license applicants. 
(f)  In the circumstances described in subsections (c), (d) and (e) of this section, the license may be revoked if the county commission determines that the change results in a failure to meet the requirements of this chapter. 
(Ord. of 11-14-2006) 
Sec. 6-197. - Change in business ownership. 
(a)  If any licensee withdraws from, sells or otherwise transfers the licensee's interest in the licensed business, the licensee shall immediately notify the county administrator and surrender the license. 
(b)  In the case of such a withdrawal, transfer, or sale, a new application shall be made as for an original license. 
(Ord. of 11-14-2006) 
Sec. 6-198. - Temporary license. 
(a)  A temporary license may be issued by the county administrator, with the approval of the county commission if, in their judgment, the denial of a temporary license would create an undue hardship such as the closing of an existing business. The temporary license shall be issued for an extra fee of $650.00 for a 90-day period with one additional 90-day extension, if needed. 
(b)  A temporary license may be revoked, with or without cause, by the county commission at any time, and the grant or denial of a temporary license shall not affect or have any bearing upon the grant or denial of a permanent license. 
(Ord. of 11-14-2006) 
Sec. 6-199. - Suspension/revocation. 
(a)  A license may be suspended or revoked by the county commission for any violation of this chapter and/or other county ordinances, for any violation of state or federal law, for any material misrepresentation or omission in the application for the license, or if the licensee or the licensed business ceases to meet the eligibility requirements for license. The county administrator shall schedule a due process hearing before the county commission for any license holder alleged to have violated any provision of this article by sending at least 14 days prior to the date of the due process hearing, a certified letter to the license holder containing the date, time, and location of the hearing, the date and nature of the allegations, and the license holder's right to be represented by an attorney and to present evidence. In lieu of a certified letter, the county administrator may elect to have service perfected by personal service by a sheriff's deputy. 
(b)  The county commission is authorized to suspend the sale of liquor by the drink under any license for any emergency situation such that the county commission finds such suspension necessary for the protection of the public health, safety, or welfare. Such suspension may be made effective immediately and may remain in force until the county commission determines that the emergency is over or until the next meeting of the county commission, at which time the suspension shall cease unless it is extended by the county commission. 
(c)  A licensee, or any citizen of the county, who is dissatisfied with the decision of the county commission, may appeal to the Superior Court of Crisp County, Georgia. Any appeal from a decision of the county commission must be filed within 30 days after such decision. 
(Ord. of 11-14-2006) 
Sec. 6-200. - Automatic revocation. 
A license shall be automatically revoked by operation of law if: 
(1)  The licensee's state alcoholic beverage license is revoked, suspended, canceled or not renewed. 
(2)  The licensed business fails to properly account for, file, report and pay any excise tax levied and due under this article. 
(3)  The licensed business fails to properly account for, file, report or maintain any records or remit any license fee imposed or taxes required under this article. 
(4)  The named licensee is convicted of a felony by a court of competent jurisdiction. 
(Ord. of 11-14-2006) 
Sec. 6-201—6-205. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 3. - LOCATION 

Sec. 6-206. - Sale/service in public places. 
It shall be unlawful to furnish or dispense liquor by the drink in public places, or to be consumed in public places. 
(Ord. of 11-14-2006) 
Sec. 6-207. - Proximity restrictions. 
(a)  No person may sell or offer to sell: 
(1)  Liquor by the drink in or within 100 yards of any church building or within 200 yards of any school building, educational building, school grounds, or college campus. This subsection shall not apply at any location for which a new license is applied for if the sale of liquor by the drink was lawful at such location at any time during the 12 months immediately preceding such application, unless the location does not have adequate parking to accommodate the restaurant or private club. Adequacy of parking under this subsection shall be determined as required by Crisp County Unified Land Development Code. 
(2)  A church building in a business zoning district is defined as a freestanding structure built for and used as a church, and does not apply to commercial or retail space that has been converted to occupancy as a church. 
(3)  Liquor by the drink within 100 yards of an alcoholic treatment center owned and/or operated by the state or Crisp County. 
(4)  All persons seeking a license for liquor by the drink shall have the proximity requirements of this section (6-207), the maximum occupant loads in section 6-230(g)(3) and the property zoning verified by the Crisp County Planning Department using "Verification Form, Planning Department (Form LD-2D)." The planning director or her designee shall investigate all liquor-by-the-drink applications for conformity and report same to the county administrator on Form LD-2D for further processing of the license application. The administrator shall sign the form and maintain it as part of the official record for the license. 
(b)  Nothing contained in this article shall prohibit the licensing of the sale or distribution of liquor by the drink by: 
(1)  Bona fide private clubs, owning their own premises, subject to licensing under state law. 
(2)  For the purposes of this article, distances shall be measured by drawing a straight line from the nearest point of the outside wall conditioned (mechanically heated or cooled) space of the applicant's business establishment to the nearest point of either: 
a.  The outside wall enclosing conditioned (mechanically heated or cooled) space of a church, school, or educational building; or 
b.  The real property of a school grounds or college campus. 
(Ord. of 11-14-2006) 
Sec. 6-208—6-210. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 4. - SALES 

Sec. 6-211. - Responsibility of named licensee. 
The named licensee shall be active in the operation of the licensed business and shall be personally present on the licensed premises sufficiently to assure compliance with the provisions of this chapter. 
(Ord. of 11-14-2006) 
Sec. 6-212. - Rentals paid restricted. 
Except as otherwise provided in this section, it shall be unlawful for a licensee to enter into any agreement whereby the rental paid for the licensed premises is based in whole or in part on the volume of sales of liquor by the drink by the licensed business or whereby the renter otherwise shares in the profits or receipts from the licensed business's sale of liquor by the drink. 
(Ord. of 11-14-2006) 
Sec. 6-213. - Display of license. 
Each license issued under this chapter shall at all times be kept plainly exposed to view upon the licensed premises. 
(Ord. of 11-14-2006) 
Sec. 6-214. - Retention of records. 
(a)  Each licensee shall keep and preserve records of all alcohol and alcoholic beverages purchased and all liquor by the drink sold by the licensee and shall keep and preserve records of all food and nonalcoholic beverages purchased and sold by them. Such records shall at all times during normal business hours be open for inspection by an authorized agent of the county. Such records shall be maintained for a period of at least three years. 
(b)  All liquor-by-the-drink licensees shall file with the county administrator the following reports by 5:00 p.m. on the 20th day of the month immediately following the end of each calendar month for which the report is filed: 
(1)  "Food Sales and Alcoholic Beverage Sales Affidavit (Form LD-3)." This is a record of the gross receipts from food sales and alcoholic beverage sales for the monthly reporting period. 
(2)  Certified copies of the licensee's monthly state sales tax reports as filed with the state department of revenue for the monthly reporting period. 
(3)  Any other documents, reports, records, or books as shall be required by the county commission to confirm the accuracy of the reported information. 
(Ord. of 11-14-2006) 
Sec. 6-215. - Knowledge of chapter provisions. 
Every licensee shall, prior to applying for a license, read and familiarize himself with the provisions of this article and an application shall constitute a certification by the applicant that he has done so. Every licensee shall maintain a copy of this article on the licensed premises and shall instruct each employee engaged in the sale or handling of alcoholic beverages on the relevant provisions of this article. 
(Ord. of 11-14-2006) 
Sec. 6-216. - Sales to underage persons prohibited. 
Furnishing to, purchase of or possession of [by] persons under 21 years of age of liquor by the drink (or any form of alcohol) shall be controlled by state law O.C.G.A. § 3-3-23. Additionally, any alleged violation of this subsection by a license holder, or its or his employee(s), shall result in a due process hearing before the county commission being called by the county chairman to determine if a license should be suspended or revoked. 
(Ord. of 11-14-2006) 
Sec. 6-217. - Days of sales prohibited. 
(a)  No licensee shall permit the sale of alcoholic beverages on any day or any time when such sales are prohibited by state law. 
(b)  The sale of liquor by the drink shall be lawful during the polling hours of any election. 
(c)  No licensee shall permit the sale of liquor by the drink between the hours of 1:00 a.m. Sunday and 12:30 p.m., Sunday or between the hours of 12:00 midnight Sunday and 8:00 a.m. Monday. 
(Ord. of 11-14-2006; Ord. of 11-12-2014(2)) 
Sec. 6-218. - Sales to intoxicated persons; gambling; disorderly conduct. 
(a)  No licensee shall permit the sale of liquor by the drink to any person who is in a state of noticeable intoxication or allow persons who are noticeably intoxicated to congregate on licensed premises. 
(b)  No licensee shall permit any gambling, betting, illegal lottery, or other device to hazard money or other thing of value on the licensed premises, except that this prohibition shall not apply with respect to a properly licensed bingo game. 
(c)  No licensee shall permit on the licensed premises any disorderly conduct, breach of the peace, or noise or activity which is disturbing to the surrounding neighborhood. 
(Ord. of 11-14-2006) 
Sec. 6-219. - Container, storage, illumination. 
(a)  Alcoholic beverages shall be delivered to and received at licensed premises only in the original container and only in a conveyance owned and operated by a licensed wholesale dealer (or licensed common carrier acting for a wholesaler). Alcoholic beverages shall be sold at retail only as liquor by the drink on the licensed premises. 
(b)  A retail licensee shall store alcoholic beverages only on the licensed premises and at no other place. All stock shall be available at all times for inspection by an authorized agent of the county. Any alcoholic beverages found in any retail licensee's stock, which were not received from a wholesaler licensed to make deliveries in the county, shall be subject to immediate confiscation. 
(c)  The exterior of each building in which alcoholic beverages are sold for consumption on the premises shall contain sufficient lighting so that all sides of the building and all entrances thereto are clearly visible at all times. 
(Ord. of 11-14-2006) 
Sec. 6-220. - Cleanliness of premises; inspections. 
All licensed premises shall be kept clean and in proper sanitary condition and in full compliance with all regulations governing the condition of premises used for the storage and sale of food for human consumption. All licensed premises shall be open at all times for inspection by authorized agents of the county. 
(Ord. of 11-14-2006) 
Sec. 6-221. - Employees of on-premises consumption liquor-by-the-drink licensees; alcohol service permit required. 
(a)  The following regulations regarding employees shall apply to all establishments holding a license for liquor by the drink on the premises: 
(1)  No person shall be employed by an establishment holding a license hereunder until such person has been issued a permit indicating that such person is eligible for this employment. However, a seven-day grace period shall be given from the date of employment until the permit is issued. The permit shall be provisional until the sheriff has had the applicant fingerprinted, photographed and cleared by the sheriff's department after a computerized background check. If the applicant's background check reveals a record that would make the employee ineligible to keep a permit, the sheriff shall revoke the permit. The permit issued to a person under this section shall be an alcohol service permit, which shall be issued only to a person who must be at least 18 years of age and who sells, serves or dispenses liquor by the drink, or is employed as a manager, host, hostess, doorman or bouncer in such establishment. A permit shall be valid for a two-year period, and shall be renewed on or before its expiration. All persons seeking employment at establishments holding a license for liquor by the drink on the premises shall complete an "Alcohol Service Permit Application (Form LD-4)" and a Georgia Bureau of Investigation, Georgia Crime Information Center consent form. 
(2)  The sheriff or his designee shall investigate all alcohol service permit applications made pursuant to this section. The sheriff may refuse to issue an alcohol service permit to any proposed employee who: 
a.  Has been convicted of a felony within a period of five years immediately prior to the date upon which the alcohol service permit application was made. 
b.  Has been convicted of two or more misdemeanors within two years immediately preceding the alcohol service permit application. Misdemeanors will be defined as violations other than minor traffic violations such as speeding, stop sign, failure to yield, following too close and etc. The two convictions for misdemeanor violations for which the violator was convicted shall have arisen at different times. 
c.  Has been convicted within a period of five years immediately preceding the application of any of the following offenses: 
1.  Pandering, prostitution or soliciting prostitution; 
2.  Gambling; 
3.  Illegal sale of controlled substance or narcotic; 
d.  This subsection shall apply with respect to the laws of this state, other states, the United States, and other countries. A plea of nolo contendere or the forfeiture of a bond shall be considered a conviction for the purposes of this subsection. 
(3)  A permit shall be issued provisionally in the first seven days of employment upon a signed application and payment of the application fee having been filed with the sheriff, until a search of the criminal record of the applicant has been completed. The application fee shall be $100.00, as currently set by the county commission; said amount may be changed from time to time at the discretion of the Board of Commissioners of Crisp County. Such application shall include, but shall not be limited to, the name, date of birth and prior arrest record of the applicant, though the fact of an arrest record shall be used for investigative purposes only, and shall give rise to no presumption or inference of guilt. Due to the inclusion of arrest information, these applications shall be regarded as confidential and shall not be produced for public inspection without a court order. 
(4)  The sheriff shall have a complete and exhaustive search made relative to any police record of the person fingerprinted or cleared. In the event there is no record of a violation of this article, the sheriff shall issue a permit to the employee, stating that the person is eligible for employment. If it is found that the person fingerprinted or cleared is not eligible for employment, the sheriff shall notify by letter the applicant and the employer that this person is not eligible for employment. 
(5)  It shall be the duty of all persons holding any license to sell liquor by the drink to file with the sheriff as part of their liquor-by-the-drink license renewal application the name of the establishment, the license number and a list of all employees, with their most recent local addresses and telephone numbers, and social security numbers. An applicant for an initial license shall furnish the same information prior to the date when on-premises consumption sales are authorized to begin. 
(6)  All permits issued through administrative error or through an error in completion of a background investigation can be terminated by the sheriff. 
(7)  This section shall not be construed to include employees whose duties are limited solely to those of delivery driver, busboy, cook, or dishwasher. 
(8)  No licensee shall allow any employee required to hold a permit to work on the licensed premises unless the licensee has on file, on the premises, a clearly legible copy of the current, valid permit of each such employee. The employee must keep the original permit on his person when at work in a licensed establishment, though it need not be publicly displayed. 
(9)  In the event that any permit holder leaves the employ of a licensed establishment, the licensee shall immediately notify the sheriff's department. 
(10)  All permits issued hereunder remain the property of the county and shall be produced for inspection upon the demand of any officer of the sheriff's department or a state law enforcement officer with jurisdiction in such matters. 
(11)  The sheriff may revoke the permit and demand its return where the employee violates the provisions of this article or becomes one who adversely affects the public health, safety, or welfare. The first such offense shall result in a suspension of the permit for 120 days. Any subsequent offense shall result in revocation of the permit, and the employee being ineligible to reapply for such a permit. 
(12)  When any employee permit is revoked, the sheriff shall issue a letter to the permit holder, and a copy to the licensee for whom he works, stating that the person does not meet the requirements of this article. 
(13)  It shall be unlawful for an employee whose permit has been revoked and upon whom demand for return of the card has been made, to refuse to return the card, or to alter, conceal, deface, or destroy the card. 
(14)  A new search may be conducted on any person issued a permit if the sheriff receives information that warrants such a new search. If the new search reveals evidence that warrants revocation of the permit, he may revoke the permit. 
(b)  Nothing herein shall in any way be construed to limit the liability of the licensee for the conduct of its employees. Any violation of this chapter by an employee remains a violation of this chapter by the licensee, who is subject to fines, suspension, or revocation as set forth herein. 
(Ord. of 11-14-2006) 
Sec. 6-222. - Drive-through sales of alcoholic beverages prohibited. 
(a)  It shall be unlawful for any person to sell or offer for sale any alcoholic beverage within the county by means of drive-through sale. 
(b)  For purposes of this chapter, the term "drive-through sale" means the sale of alcoholic beverages by any means that allows the customer to remain in his vehicle. 
(Ord. of 11-14-2006) 
DIVISION 5. - EMPLOYMENT OF UNDERAGE PERSONS 

Sec. 6-223. - General prohibitions. 
(a)  No liquor-by-the-drink licensee shall allow any employee under the age of 18 years to dispense, sell, serve, take orders for, or handle alcoholic beverages. 
(b)  This section shall not prohibit the employment of persons under the above ages on licensed premises where such persons do not dispense, sell, serve, take orders for, or handle alcoholic beverages. 
(Ord. of 11-14-2006) 
Sec. 6-224. - Brown-bagging prohibited. 
It shall be unlawful for patrons of restaurants as defined under section 6-230 or private clubs as defined under section 6-231 to bring onto the premises their own alcoholic beverages, which is commonly known as "bring your own bottle" (BYOB) or "brown-bagging". It shall be unlawful for restaurants as defined under section 6-230 or private clubs as defined under section 6-231 to allow customers to bring onto the premises their own alcoholic beverages, which is commonly known as "bring your own bottle" (BYOB) or "brown-bagging". Note: For clarification, this paragraph prohibits "bring your own bottle" (BYOB) or "brown-bagging" at any establishment whatsoever that is open to the public. 
(Ord. of 11-14-2006) 
Sec. 6-225—6-228. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 6. - CONSUMPTION ON PREMISES 

Sec. 6-229. - Eligibility restricted—generally. 
A liquor-by-the-drink license may be granted only to a restaurant, as defined under section 6-230 and a private club as defined under section 6-231. 
(Ord. of 11-14-2006) 
Sec. 6-230. - Same—restaurant. 
To be eligible for a liquor-by-the-drink license, a restaurant shall: 
(a)  Be used and held out to the public as a place where meals prepared on the premises are regularly served to the public for adequate pay each day the establishment is open for business; 
(b)  Contain one or more public dining rooms, with adequate and sanitary kitchen facilities and refrigeration as required by the Crisp County Health Department and staff to prepare, cook and serve suitable food for its guests. 
(c)  Have the ability to serve meals prepared on the premises during any time the establishment is open for business. 
(d)  Have a valid Crisp County Health Department Food Service Permit and any other applicable local, state or federal permits, licenses, etc., required for food service establishments. 
(e)  Have at least 60 percent of its total sales comprised of the sale of food prepared on the premises and nonalcoholic beverages consumed on the premises; and for this purpose, if a restaurant makes a minimum charge, cover charge, or admission charge, or any other nonfood or nonalcoholic beverage charge, the amount so charged shall not be counted in computing total sales and shall not be counted as a food or beverage sale; 
(f)  Have a permanent seating capacity at tables, not counting bar stools, of at least 25 persons. 
(g)  The occupancy load for purposes of this section must meet the following criteria: 
(1)  The square footage of the interior area of the restaurant, which is enclosed and under roof and is conditioned air space, shall be determined using a set of building plans showing the fixed and other seating and tables. 
(2)  The food preparation service areas (kitchen, buffet and salad bar areas), storage, the preparation area behind bars, restrooms and all connecting hallways shall be removed from the total square footage of the floor space. 
(3)  The maximum occupant load for the remaining areas shall be calculated in accordance with the building code and life safety code as follows: 
a.  The assembly area where restaurant seating is located shall be calculated using 15 square feet per person. 
b.  The waiting area at the entrance/exit shall be calculated using three square feet per person. The number of occupants allowed in the calculation for waiting area cannot exceed 50 percent of the occupant load of the assembly area in subsection 6-230(g)(3)a., above. 
c.  An additional area for live entertainment and dancing shall be calculated using seven square feet per person. The number of occupants allowed in the calculation for this additional area cannot exceed 20 percent of the occupant load of the assembly areas in subsection 6-230(g)(3)a., above. 
d.  The county commission may consider a request for consumption on the premises of a deck or patio attached or adjacent to the principal restaurant assembly area. If such a request is granted, it does not alter the calculation of the maximum occupant load. 
e.  The establishment's "Certificate of Occupant Load (Form LD-2C)" issued by the county administrator for each location shall be posted for public view at all times. 
(h)  Maintain at all times the number of tables, chairs, and booths for patrons in substantially the same general configuration as submitted on the set of building plans used to determine the occupancy load. Nothing herein shall prohibit the temporary placing of tables together to accommodate a larger dining party, provided the total number of tables, chairs and booths available for patron use in the assembly area where restaurant seating is located must equal the number shown on the building plans submitted for occupancy purposes, with adequate space between them for normal movement of patrons and employees. The intent of this provision is to prohibit the removal at any time of the restaurant's seating or table capacity, as shown for occupancy load purposes, to accommodate more than the allowed number of patrons within the assembly area of the restaurant. 
(Ord. of 11-14-2006) 
Sec. 6-231. - Private club. 
(a)  In order to be eligible for a liquor-by-the-drink license, a private club must be a veterans organization, fraternal organization or other nonprofit organization all of which must be incorporated, and: 
(1)  The local chapter has been in existence at least five years prior to the filing of its application for a license. 
(2)  Have at least 40 regular dues-paying members. (Exceptions may be made on a case-by-case basis by the Crisp County Board of Commissioners.) 
(3)  Be organized and operated exclusively for pleasure, recreation and other nonprofit purposes. 
(4)  Own, hire, or lease a building or space within a building for the reasonable use of its members. 
(b)  Has no member, officer, agent, or employee directly or indirectly receiving in the form of salary or other compensation any profits from the sale of alcoholic beverages beyond a fixed salary. 
(c)  No liquor-by-the-drink license shall be granted to a private club organized or operated primarily for the selling or serving of alcoholic beverages. 
(d)  Private clubs licensed under the provisions of this section shall not be required to maintain the percentage sale of food/nonalcoholic beverages as compared to alcoholic beverages, however such organization shall be subject to all regulations of this article dealing with general licensing and consumption of liquor by the drink on the premises. 
(Ord. of 11-14-2006) 
Sec. 6-232. - Ratio of alcoholic/nonalcoholic sales. 
Should the total sales from food and nonalcoholic beverages reported by any liquor-by-the-drink licensee not equal those from the sale of all alcoholic beverages for any two consecutive reporting periods, or for two nonconsecutive reporting periods in any 12-month period, the license may be suspended or revoked by the county commission after a hearing as provided for in section 6-199. 
(Ord. of 11-14-2006) 
Sec. 6-233. - Reserved. 
Sec. 6-234. - Illumination of premises, location of sales restricted. 
(a)  All restaurants, including all tables, booths, and other areas where customers are served and including all passageways for customers, shall be sufficiently well illuminated so that they may be viewed by those inside the premises. 
(b)  The sale of alcoholic beverages in any back room or side room that is not open to the general public is prohibited, except that this prohibition shall not apply with respect to: 
(1)  Private parties that have been scheduled in advance; 
(2)  Room service to hotel guests in their hotel rooms provided a properly licensed restaurant is located on the premises. 
(3)  Private clubs. 
(Ord. of 11-14-2006) 
Sec. 6-235. - Hours of sale. 
Liquor-by-the-drink licensees shall only engage in the sale and/or service of liquor by the drink between the hours of 8:00 a.m. and 12:00 a.m. Monday through Saturday and between the hours of 12:30 p.m. and 12:00 midnight Sunday, with consumption of purchased beverages on the premises until 1:00 a.m. 
(Ord. of 11-14-2006; Ord. of 11-12-2014(2)) 
Sec. 6-236. - Dancing on premises prohibited. 
Patron dancing shall be permitted at facilities licensed for liquor-by-the-drink sales only where: 
(a)  Adequate space exists. 
(b)  All fire and safety regulations are met. 
(Ord. of 11-14-2006) 
Sec. 6-237. - Removal of beverages prohibited. 
All alcoholic beverages sold by liquor-by-the-drink licensees shall be consumed only on the licensed premises. It shall be unlawful for any person to remove from the licensed premises any alcoholic beverages sold for consumption on the premises to any public streets, sidewalks or rights-of-way, or in any public or semipublic parking facility within the county. 
(Ord. of 11-14-2006) 
Sec. 6-238. - Prohibition of certain types of entertainment, attire and conduct. 
(a)  Findings; public purpose. Based on the experience of other counties and municipalities, including, but not limited to, Atlanta and Fulton County, Georgia; DeKalb County, Georgia; Richmond County, Georgia; Amarillo, Texas; Austin, Texas; Garden Grove, California; Houston, Texas; Renton, Washington; Phoenix, Arizona; Indianapolis, Indiana; St. Paul, Minnesota; Tucson, Arizona; Augusta, Georgia; LaGrange, Georgia; Dalton and Whitfield County, Georgia; Carrollton, Georgia; Smyrna, Georgia; and Ft. Lauderdale and Palm Beach, Florida, which experiences the county commission believes are relevant to the problems faced by Crisp County, the county commission takes note of the notorious and self-evident conditions attendant to the commercial exploitation of human sexuality, which do not vary greatly among generally comparable communities within our country. Moreover, it is the finding of the county commission that public nudity (either partial or total) under certain circumstances, particularly circumstances related to the sale and consumption of alcoholic beverages, begets criminal behavior and tends to create undesirable community conditions. Among the acts of criminal behavior identified with nudity and alcohol are disorderly conduct, prostitution, and drug trafficking and use. Among the undesirable community conditions identified with nudity and alcohol are depression of property values in the surrounding neighborhood, increased expenditure for and allocation of law enforcement personnel to preserve law and order, increased burden on the judicial system as a consequence of the criminal behavior hereinabove described, and acceleration of community blight by the concentration of such establishments in particular areas. Therefore, the limitation of nude conduct in establishments licensed to sell alcoholic beverages is in the public welfare and it is a matter of governmental interest, and concern to prevent the occurrence of criminal behavior and undesirable community conditions normally associated with establishments that serve alcohol and also allow and/or encourage nudity. To that end, this section is hereby adopted. 
(b)  Enactment. The following types of entertainment, attire and conduct are prohibited upon any premises licensed to sell, serve or disperse liquor by the drink. 
(1)  The employment or use of any person, in any capacity, in the sale or service of liquor by the drink while such person is unclothed or in such attire, costume or clothing, as to expose to view any portion of the female breast below the top of the areola or any portion of the male or female pubic hair, anus, cleft or the buttocks, vulva and genitals. 
(2)  Live entertainment where any person appears in the manner described in subsection (1) of this subsection. 
(Ord. of 11-14-2006) 
Sec. 6-239. - Pricing of liquor by the drink. 
(a)  This section shall be construed to cover, include and apply to liquor by the drink. 
(b)  No licensee or holder of a license to sell liquor by the drink, or employee or agent of a licensee, shall: 
(1)  Offer to deliver any free liquor by the drink. 
(2)  Deliver more than one liquor drink to one person at one time, or allow any patron to possess more than one liquor drink at one time. 
(3)  Sell, offer to sell, or deliver to any person or group of persons two or more or an unlimited number of liquor drinks during any set period of time at a fixed price, except at private functions not open to the public. 
(4)  Sell, offer to sell, or deliver liquor by the drink to any person or group of persons on any one day at prices less than those charged the general public on that day, except at private functions not open to the public. 
(5)  Sponsor, conduct, encourage or allow on the licensed premises any game or contest or promotion which either: 
a.  Involves the drinking of alcoholic beverages or the awarding of alcoholic beverages as the prize; or 
b.  Has as its primary purpose the increasing of the consumption of alcoholic beverages on the premises. 
(6)  Sell, offer to sell, or deliver to a customer liquor by the drink in any container other than a glass or plastic cup. 
(7)  Sell, offer to sell, deliver, or allow any alcoholic beverage to be inserted into the mouth of a customer in any manner by anyone other than by the customer. 
(8)  Charge any minimum charge, cover charge, admission charge, or any other non-food or nonalcoholic beverage charge that discriminates on the basis of gender, race, age, creed, or national origin. 
(9)  Deny entry or service to any person at any time on the basis of gender, race, age, creed, or national origin. 
(c)  No provision of this section shall be construed to prohibit licensees from offering free food or entertainment at any time, or to prohibit any hotel or motel from offering room services to registered guests. 
(Ord. of 11-14-2006) 
Sec. 6-240. - Misrepresentation of alcoholic beverages. 
It shall be unlawful for licensees under this article or their agents to add to the contents of a bottle or to refill empty bottles or in any other manner to misrepresent the quantity, quality or brand name of any alcoholic beverage. 
(Ord. of 11-14-2006) 
Sec. 6-241—6-243. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 7. - EXCISE TAX ON MIXED DRINKS 

Sec. 6-244. - Imposition. 
There is imposed upon the sale of liquor by the drink in the county a tax in the amount of three percent of the purchase price of each drink to the consumer. Each licensee shall be allowed a deduction of three percent of the amount of taxes collected as reimbursement for collection of such taxes, provided that such tax is not delinquent at the time of payment. A record of each sale shall be made in writing and maintained for inspection by any authorized agent of the county. 
(Ord. of 11-14-2006) 
Sec. 6-245. - Collection. 
Every liquor-by-the-drink licensee shall collect the tax imposed by this article from purchasers of all such drinks. The licensee shall furnish such information as may be required by the county commission to facilitate the collection of the tax. In all cases where the purchase is by deferred payment or credit, the licensee becomes liable for the collection and payment of the tax at the time of delivery of such drink to the purchasers. 
(Ord. of 11-14-2006) 
Sec. 6-246. - Payment to county. 
(a)  Each licensee shall pay over the amount of taxes collected and coming due under this article in every calendar month to the county not later than the 20th day of the following calendar month. 
(b)  On or before the 20th day of each month, a return shall be filed with the county administrator for the preceding month by each licensee liable for the payment of tax under this article. Returns shall be in a form the county administrator may specify and shall show the licensee's gross receipts from the sale of liquor by the drink and the amount of taxes collected or coming due thereon. Report shall be made on the "Gross Receipts & Excise Tax Report (Form LD-5)." 
(Ord. of 11-14-2006) 
DIVISION 8. - EFFECTIVE DATE; SEVERABILITY; SHORT TITLE 

Sec. 6-247. - Effective date. 
This article shall become effective on December 1, 2006. 
(Ord. of 11-14-2006) 
Sec. 6-248—6-250. - Reserved. 
Sec. 6-251. - Provisions herein are severable. 
Should any provision herein be declared unconstitutional or illegal by a court of competent jurisdiction, the remaining provisions shall remain of full force and effect. 
(Ord. of 11-14-2006) 
Sec. 6-252. - Short title. 
This article shall be known as and may be cited as the "Crisp County 2006 Liquor by the Drink Ordinance." 
(Ord. of 11-14-2006) 
Chapter 10 - AMUSEMENTS AND ENTERTAINMENTS[1]
