ARTICLE II. - WATER RATES AND SERVICE RULES 

Sec. 66-31. - Rate schedule. 
(a)  Effective July 1, 1996, and the duration of the loan from USDA Rural Development (RD) regarding the construction of the county water system, there is adopted the following monthly water rate schedules for the county: 
WATER RATE SCHEDULE 

 
(b)  The rate schedule set forth in subsection (a) of this section contemplates a single user, such as a one-family dwelling, a one-farm dwelling with appurtenances, or one commercial operation. 
(c)  Extraordinary circumstances, such as multiple dwelling units, industrial users and fire protection shall be governed by special contract agreements made by the board of commissioners on recommendation of the county engineer except as otherwise provided in this article. 
(Res. of 7-1-1996, § 1; Res. of 6-16-2006, §§ 1, 2; Res. of 5-14-2013(1), § 1) 
Sec. 66-32. - Application for water service; security deposit. 
The consumer shall make application for water service, in person, at the office of the county water system and at the same time shall make a cash security deposit for water service as follows: 

 
(Res. of 7-1-1996, § 2) 
Sec. 66-33. - Tap fee. 
(a)  In addition to the security deposit provided in section 66-32, each customer subscribing to use the water service of the county shall pay a connection fee (tap fee) as follows times the number of connections desired for water service: 

 
(b)  The fees stated in subsection (a) of this section shall take effect July 1, 1996. 
(Res. of 7-1-1996, § 3) 
Sec. 66-34. - Minimum charges. 
The minimum charge, as provided in the rate schedule in section 66-31, shall be made for such connection subscribed for under this article. Water furnished for a given lot shall be used on that lot only and, except for fire protection, the county shall not under any condition furnish water free of charge to anyone. 
(Res. of 7-1-1996, § 4) 
Sec. 66-35. - County's responsibility and liability. 
The county shall run a service line from its distribution line to the property line, where the distribution line exists or is to be constructed, and runs immediately adjacent and parallel to the property to be served. No service charge, other than the connection fee referred to in section 66-33, will be made. 
(1)  The county may make connections to service other properties not adjacent to its lines upon payment of reasonable costs for the extensions of its distribution lines as may be required to render such service. 
(2)  The county may install its meter at or near the property line or, at the county's option, on the consumer's property within three feet of the property line. 
(3)  The county reserves the right to refuse service unless the consumer's lines or pipes are installed in such a manner as to prevent cross connections or backflow. 
(4)  Under normal conditions, the consumer will be notified of any anticipated interruptions of service by the county. 
(Res. of 7-1-1996, § 5) 
Sec. 66-36. - Consumer's responsibility and liability. 
Water furnished by the county shall be used for consumption by the consumer, members of his household and employees only. The consumer shall not sell water to any other person or permit any other person to use such water. Water shall not be used for irrigation, fire protection, nor other purposes, except when water is available in sufficient quantity without interfering with the regular domestic consumption in the area served. Disregard for this rule shall be sufficient cause for refusal and/or discontinuance of service. 
(1)  Where a meter or meter box is placed on the premises of a consumer, a suitable place shall be provided by the consumer therefor, unobstructed and accessible at all times to the meter reader. 
(2)  The consumer shall furnish and maintain a private cutoff valve on the consumer's side of the meter. 
(3)  The consumer's piping and apparatus shall be installed and maintained by the consumer at the consumer's expense, in a safe and efficient manner, and in accordance with the sanitary regulations of the state health department. 
(4)  In order to be received as a consumer and entitled to receive water from the county water system, all applicants must offer proof that any private wells located on their property are not physically connected to the lines of the county water system and all applicants by becoming consumers of the county, covenant and agree that so long as they continue to be consumers of the county they will not permit the connection of any private wells on their property to the county water system. 
(5)  Prior to the installation of water lines, a developer is required to provide the county with an acceptable layout plan and specifications for construction utility and specifications for construction utilizing and tendering an acceptable water line easement. During construction, it is necessary for the county to make periodic inspections and to observe the pressure testing when water is placed in lines. Upon approval by the county of the plans, specifications, tests and acceptance of the water line easement, the county will accept the water mains for maintenance and will operate same in accordance with the rights granted in the respective water line easement subject to all other rights and reservations contained in this article. The substance of this provision was adopted by the board of commissioners by its action of May 14, 1996, and shall continue and be in full force and effect upon adoption of this article. 
(Res. of 7-1-1996, § 6) 
Sec. 66-37. - Access to premises and extensions of system. 
(a)  Duly authorized agents of the county shall have access at all hours to the premises of the consumer for the purpose of installing or removing county property, inspection of piping, reading and testing meters, or for any other purpose in connection with the water service and its facilities. 
(b)  Extensions to the water system shall be granted only when the consumer shall grant or convey, or shall cause to be granted or conveyed, to the county an acceptable permanent easement or right-of-way across any property traversed by the water lines. 
(Res. of 7-1-1996, § 7) 
Sec. 66-38. - Change of occupancy. 
Not less than three days' notice must be given in person or in writing at the office of the county water system to discontinue water service or to change occupancy. The outgoing party shall be responsible for all water consumed up to the time of departure or the time specified for departure, whichever period is longer. The new occupant shall apply for water service within 48 hours after occupying the premises and failure to do so will make him liable for paying for the water consumed since the last meter reading. 
(Res. of 7-1-1996, § 8) 
Sec. 66-39. - Bill collecting; penalties for nonpayment. 
(a)  Bills to customers of water service shall be mailed out on such day or days of each month as may be determined as desirable by the county. The failure of water users to pay charges duly imposed shall result in the automatic imposition of the following penalties: 
(1)  Nonpayment within ten days from the due date will be subject to a penalty of $5.00. 
(2)  Nonpayment within 40 days from the date due will result in the water being shut off from the water user's property. 
(3)  Nonpayment for 60 days after original due date will allow the county, in addition to all other rights and remedies, to terminate agreement, and in such event, the water user shall not be entitled to receive, nor the county obligated to supply, any water under this article. 
(b)  Water service shall not be reconnected until the customer's delinquent bill, including penalty, has been paid in full. Should such customer thereafter desire to be reconnected to the water system, a reconnection charge of $35.00 shall be collected. Bills shall be paid at the office of the county water system or other designated locations and a failure to receive bills or notices shall not prevent such bills from becoming delinquent or relieve the consumer from payment of same. 
(c)  A minimum service charge of $10.00 will be made when county employees are called upon by a consumer to perform services. 
(Res. of 7-1-1996, § 9) 
Sec. 66-40. - Suspension of service. 
(a)  When water services are discontinued and all bills are paid, the security deposit shall be refunded to the consumer by the county. 
(b)  Upon discontinuance of service for nonpayment of bills, the security deposit will be applied by the county toward settlement of the account. Any balance will be refunded to the consumer; however, if the security deposit is insufficient to cover the bill, the county may proceed to collect the balance in the usual way provided by law for collection of debts. 
(c)  Service disconnected for nonpayment of bills will be restored only after bills are paid in full, such security deposit as may be required by the board of commissioners is made, and a service charge of $35.00 is paid for each meter reconnected. 
(d)  The county reserves a right to discontinue water service without notice for the following additional reasons: 
(1)  To prevent fraud or abuse. 
(2)  The consumer's willful disregard of the county's rules. 
(3)  Emergency repairs. 
(4)  Insufficiency of the water supply due to circumstances beyond the county's control. 
(5)  Legal processes. 
(6)  Direction of public authorities. 
(7)  Strike, riot, fire, flood, war or unavoidable accident. 
(Res. of 7-1-1996, § 10) 
Sec. 66-41. - Complaints; adjustments. 
If a consumer believes his bill is in error, he shall present his claim, in person, at the office of the county water system before the bill becomes delinquent. Such claim, if made after the bill has become delinquent, shall not be effective in preventing discontinuance of services provided under this article. The consumer may pay such bill under protest and such payment shall not prejudice his claim. 
(1)  The county will make a special water meter reading at the request of a consumer for a fee of $10.00; however, if such special reading discloses that the meter was overread, no charge will be made. 
(2)  Water meters will be tested at the request of the consumer upon payment to the county of the actual costs of making the test; however, if the meter is found to overregister beyond three percent of the correct volume, no charge will be made. 
(3)  If the seal of a meter is broken by other than the county's representative or if the meter fails to register correctly or is stopped for any cause, the consumer shall pay an amount estimated from the record of his previous bills and/or from other proper data. 
(Res. of 7-1-1996, § 11) 
Sec. 66-42. - Floodplain prohibition. 
Structures constructed within the floodplain area, as specified in the flood damage prevention ordinance adopted by the board of commissioners on April 4, 1996, and the Sumter County Board of Commissioners on March 12, 1996, shall not be connected to the water system. 
(Res. of 7-1-1996, § 12) 
Secs. 66-43—66-70. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE III. - WATER AND SEWER SERVICES PROVIDED BY THE CITY OF CORDELE 

Sec. 66-71. - Rate schedule. 
The rates for water and sewer services provided by the City of Cordele in the unincorporated areas of the county shall be according to the fee schedule adopted by the Cordele City Commission and on file in the City of Cordele Clerk's Office. 
(Res. of 1-9-2001, § 2) 
Sec. 66-72. - Application for water and sewer service. 
The customer shall make application for water service, and sewer service where provided, in person, at the Cordele City Hall, 501 North Seventh Street, Cordele, Georgia, and shall make a security deposit for such service as provided by the fee schedule adopted by the Cordele City Commission on file in the City of Cordele Clerk's Office. 
(Res. of 1-9-2001, § 3) 
Sec. 66-73. - Meter and tap fees; commencement of service. 
In addition to the security deposit provided in section 66-72, each customer subscribing after January 1, 2000, to use the water (and sewer, if applicable) service provided by this article shall pay meter and tap fees as provided by the fee schedule adopted by the Cordele City Commission on file in the City of Cordele Clerk's Office. Users must come on to the system within three days after the water meter/tap is installed and shall be billed for availability on a monthly basis. 
(Res. of 1-9-2001, § 4) 
Sec. 66-74. - Minimum charges. 
The minimum charge, as provided in the fee schedule adopted by the Cordele City Commission on file in the City of Cordele Clerk's Office, shall be made for each connection subscribed for. Water (and sewer service where applicable) furnished for a given lot or location shall be used on that lot or location only and, except for fire protection, the City of Cordele shall not for any reason whatsoever furnish water free of charge to anyone. If a customer is approved for installment payments to pay for the water meter fee and/or sewer tap fee, the maximum time to complete such installment payments shall not be longer than six months after approval of same. 
(Res. of 1-9-2001, § 5) 
Sec. 66-75. - Fire protection. 
The City of Cordele will not provide fire protection for unincorporated areas of the county; however, the county fire department may use water from the system regulated by this article for fire protection only. Such use by the county fire department is subject to water availability, and shall be loaded into fire apparatus only at designated fire hydrants to which a backflow prevention device and meter, which has been installed by the city, or a backflow prevention device and meter which has been installed on the county's firefighting apparatus that withdraws water. 
(Res. of 1-9-2001, § 6) 
Sec. 66-76. - City's responsibility and liability. 
The City of Cordele shall run service lines from its distribution line (and sewer line if applicable) to the property line where the lines exist or may be constructed. No service charge, other than the connection fee referred to in section 66-73, will be made. 
(1)  The city may make connections to service other properties not adjacent to its lines upon payment of costs for the extensions according to the fee schedule adopted by the Cordele City Commission on file in the City of Cordele Clerk's Office. 
(2)  The city may install its meter at or near the property line, or, at the city's option, on the customer's property within three feet of the property line. 
(3)  The city shall refuse service unless the customer's water line provides a backflow prevention device approved by the city at or near the customer's side of the meter. 
(4)  The city will make a reasonable effort to notify the customer of any anticipated interruptions of service. 
(Res. of 1-9-2001, § 7) 
Sec. 66-77. - Customer's responsibility and liability. 
Water furnished by the City of Cordele shall be used for consumption by the customer, members of his household and employees only. The customer shall not sell or give water to any other person or permit any other person to use such water. Water shall not be used for irrigation, fire protection, nor other purposes, except when water is available in sufficient quantity without interfering with the regular domestic consumption in the area served. Disregarding this rule, in addition to penalties for violation of this article, shall be sufficient cause for refusal and/or discontinuance of service. 
(1)  Plumbing permits from the county and inspections by the county are required on all new or renovated construction involving water and sewer service and new water meters installed, including meters for yard irrigation. Appropriate backflow devices shall be required. 
(2)  When a meter or meter boxes are placed on the premises of a customer, a suitable place shall be provided by the customer therefor, unobstructed and accessible at all times to the meter reader. 
(3)  The customer shall furnish and maintain a private cut-off valve on the customer's side of the meter. 
(4)  The customer's piping and apparatus shall be installed and maintained by the customer at the customer's expense, in a safe and efficient manner, and in accordance with the adopted plumbing codes and other applicable ordinances of the county. 
(5)  In order to be received as a customer and entitled to receive water from the water system controlled by this article, all applicants must offer proof that any private wells located on their property are not physically connected to the lines of such water system, and all applicants, by becoming customers of the city, covenant and agree that so long as they continue to be customers of the city they will not permit the connection of any private wells on their property to the water system controlled by this article. 
(6)  Prior to the installation of water lines, a developer is required to provide the city with an acceptable layout plan and specification for construction of water lines (and sewer lines, if applicable) in the proposed development. During construction, it is necessary and required that the city make periodic inspections and to observe the pressure testing when water is placed in lines. Upon approval by the city of the plan, specifications, tests and acceptance of the water line easement (and the sewer line easement, if applicable) the city will accept the water lines for maintenance and will operate same in accordance with the rights granted in the respective water line easements subject to all other rights and reservations contained in this article. 
(Res. of 1-9-2001, § 8) 
Sec. 66-78. - Access to premises; extensions of systems. 
(a)  Duly authorized agents of the city, designated by the city manager, shall have access at all hours to the premises of the customer for the purpose of installing or removing property of the City of Cordele, inspection of piping, reading and testing meters, and for any other purpose in connection with the water and sewer service and its facilities. 
(b)  Extensions to the system shall be granted only with a customer who shall grant or convey, or cause to be granted or conveyed, to the City of Cordele, an acceptable permanent easement or a right-of-way across any property traversed by water and sewer lines. 
(Res. of 1-9-2001, § 9) 
Sec. 66-79. - Changes of occupancy. 
Not less than three days' notice must be given in person or in writing at the Cordele City Hall, 501 North Seventh Street, Cordele, Georgia, to discontinue water service or to change occupancy. The outgoing party shall be responsible for all water consumed up to the time of departure or the time specified for departure, whichever period is longer. The new occupant shall apply for water service within 48 hours after occupying the premises. In addition to penalties of violations of this article, this section will make the new occupant liable for paying for the water consumed since the last meter reading. 
(Res. of 1-9-2001, § 10) 
Sec. 66-80. - Bill collecting; penalties for nonpayment. 
Bills of customers of water service (and sewer service, where applicable) shall be mailed out on such day or days of each month as may be determined as desirable by the city. The failure of utility users to pay charges duly imposed shall result in automatic imposition of the following penalties: 
(1)  Payment after the due date will be subject to a penalty in an amount provided in the fee schedule adopted by the Cordele City Commission on file in the City of Cordele Clerk's Office. 
(2)  Nonpayment after the shutoff date will result in the water being shut off from the water user's property. 
(3)  Water service shall not be reconnected until the customer's delinquent bill, including penalties, has been paid in full. Should such customer thereafter desire to be reconnected to the water system, a reconnection charge, in an amount determined from time to time by the city commission, shall be collected. Bills shall be paid at the Cordele City Hall, 501 North Seventh Street, Cordele, Georgia, or at the mailing address printed upon the bill. Failure to receive bills or notices mailed to the billing address shall not prevent such bills from becoming delinquent or relieve the customer from payment of the same. The city may, but is not required, on a case by case basis, allow a delinquent bill to be paid on an installment schedule. 
(4)  When city employees are called upon by a customer to perform services, a fee will be charged in an amount provided in the fee schedule adopted by the Cordele City Commission on file in the City of Cordele Clerk's Office. 
(Res. of 1-9-2001, § 11) 
Sec. 66-81. - Suspension of service. 
(a)  When water services are discontinued and all are bills paid, the security deposit will be refunded to the customer by the City of Cordele. 
(b)  Upon discontinuance of service for nonpayment of bills for water service, the security deposit may be applied by the City of Cordele toward settlement of the account. Any balance will be refunded to the customer; however, if the security deposit is insufficient to cover the bill, the city may proceed to collect the balance in any way provided by law for collection of debts. 
(c)  Service discontinued for nonpayment of bills for water service will be restored only after the bills are paid in full, such security deposit as required by this article is made, and a service charge paid for each meter reconnected, such charge being in an amount set from time to time by the Cordele City Commission, and being the same as charged to customers within the City of Cordele. 
(d)  The City of Cordele reserves the right to discontinue service provided by this article without notice for the following additional reasons: 
(1)  To prevent fraud or abuse. 
(2)  The customer's willful disregard of rules provided by this article. 
(3)  Emergency repairs. 
(4)  Insufficiency of the water supply due to circumstances beyond the control of the City of Cordele. 
(5)  Legal processes. 
(6)  Direction of public authorities. 
(7)  Strike, riot, fire, flood, war, unavoidable accident or force majeure. 
(Res. of 1-9-2001, § 12) 
Sec. 66-82. - Specific article violations. 
It shall be a violation of this article to fail to abide by any provision of this article, and in addition, it shall be a violation of this article to: 
(1)  Tamper with meters, lines and devices belonging to the systems regulated by this article or required by this article. 
(2)  Reconnect services when services have been discontinued or turned off for nonpayment of bills. 
(3)  Use of any bypass, device, scheme or false representation to avoid payment in full for water and sewer services. 
(4)  Using a false, fictitious or unauthorized name for connection of services to avoid payment for charges for services previously used. 
(5)  Use of the name of a minor for connection of services. 
(6)  Use of a hose, pipe or other device to obtain or render unauthorized water service. 
(Res. of 1-9-2001, § 13) 
Sec. 66-83. - Designation of representatives; citations. 
The City Manager of the City of Cordele and his designees shall carry out the provisions of this article and shall be authorized to issue citations for violations of this article. Citations shall be returnable to the magistrate court of the county. The citation forms shall be provided by such court. Use of citations shall be as provided by O.C.G.A. § 15-10-63, or as such section may hereafter be amended. If the judge of such court requires that a prosecuting attorney must be provided in a particular case, the City Attorney for the City of Cordele shall provide such prosecution. 
(Res. of 1-9-2001, § 14) 
Sec. 66-84. - Violations. 
Any person found guilty of a violation of this article shall, upon conviction in the magistrate court of the county, be punished by the judge of such court within the limits provided by O.C.G.A. § 15-10-60, or as such section may hereafter be amended. 
(Res. of 1-9-2001, § 15) 
Sec. 66-85. - Complaints; adjustments. 
If the customer believes his bill is in error, he shall present his claim, in person, at the Cordele City Hall, 501 North Seventh Street, Cordele, Georgia, to the person designated by the city manager for hearing utility complaints. Such claim shall be presented by the customer before his bill becomes delinquent. Such claim, if made after the bill has become delinquent, shall not be effective in preventing discontinuance of services provided under this article. The customer may pay such bill under protest and the payment shall not prejudice his claim. 
(1)  The city will make a special water meter reading at the request of a customer for a fee of $10.00; however, if such special reading discloses that the meter was overread, no charge shall be made. 
(2)  Water meters will be tested at the request of the customer upon payment to the city of the actual costs of making the test; however, if the meter is found to overregister beyond three percent of the correct volume, no charge shall be made. 
(3)  If the seal of a meter is broken by other than the city's representative or if the meter fails to register correctly or is stopped for any cause, the customer shall pay an amount estimated from the record of his previous bills and/or from other data considered proper under the circumstances by the City of Cordele. 
(4)  If an estimation of water usage is necessary because of a major leak, such estimation shall be in accordance with the fee schedule adopted by the Cordele City Commission on file in the City of Cordele Clerk's Office. 
(Res. of 1-9-2001, § 16) 
Sec. 66-86. - Floodplain prohibition. 
Structures constructed within the floodplain area, as specified in the floodplain damage prevention ordinance adopted by the board of commissioners on April 4, 1996, shall not be connected to the utilities regulated by this ordinance, unless the structures to be served were constructed prior to the effective date of such ordinance or has been constructed in compliance with the ordinance. 
(Res. of 1-9-2001, § 17) 
Sec. 66-87. - No waiver of service delivery strategies laws. 
Notwithstanding any other provision of this article, no fees, rates, penalties or other charges to customers located outside the geographic boundaries of the City of Cordele shall be arbitrarily higher than the fees charged to the customers receiving such service which are located within the geographic boundaries of the City of Cordele and the board of commissioners specifically reserves its right to contest any such differentials as provided by O.C.G.A. § 36-70-24(2). The board of commissioners expressly finds that the city's present schedule of fees, rates, penalties and other charges to customers outside the geographic boundaries of the City of Cordele is not arbitrarily higher than the schedule of the same for customers within the geographic boundaries of the City of Cordele. 
(Res. of 1-9-2001, § 18) 
Secs. 66-88—66-100. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE IV. - ON-SITE SEWAGE MANAGEMENT SYSTEMS 

Sec. 66-101. - Definitions. 
The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this article, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
On-site sewage management system means a sewage management system other than a public or community sewage treatment system, whether serving single or multiple buildings, mobile homes, recreational vehicles, residences or other facilities designed or used for human occupancy or congregation. Included are conventional septic tank systems, privies, experimental and alternative on-site sewage management systems, portable toilets and other systems that may be approved by the county board of health. 
(Res. of 6-9-1987, § 2.01) 
Cross reference— Definitions generally, § 1-2. 
Sec. 66-102. - Violation. 
Any person violating any of the provisions of this article shall be tried in the magistrate's court of the county, and if convicted, shall be punished as provided in section 1-11. 
(Res. of 6-9-1987, § 7.01) 
Sec. 66-103. - System required. 
Where public or community sewage treatment systems are not available, the owner, or lessee or agent thereof of every building, residence or property, designed, used or intended to be used for human occupancy or congregation, shall provide an approved on-site sewage management system sufficient for persons normally expected to use or frequent the building, residence or other property for two hours or more. 
(Res. of 6-9-1987, § 3.01) 
Sec. 66-104. - Standards required. 
New installations of on-site sewage management systems shall meet all standards and provisions, except the subdivision portions thereof, set forth by the county board of health and the state department of human resources. No person may begin the physical development of a lot or structure thereon, where an on-site sewage management system will be utilized, nor install a new on-site management system, without first having applied for and obtained from the county board of health, a construction permit for the installation. No person may cover or use an on-site sewage management system until final inspection has been made by the county board of health to determine compliance with the provisions and standards of construction, and written approval has been issued by the county board of health. 
(Res. of 6-9-1987, § 4.01; Res. of 3-14-1989, § 4.01) 
Sec. 66-105. - Subdivision and mobile home parks. 
No person may sell, offer for sale, lease, rent, begin construction or otherwise begin the physical development of a subdivision or mobile home park where public or community sewage treatment systems are not available or contemplated to be available to serve the proposed development until proposals and plans for the water supply and sewage disposal method to be provided or installed have been submitted to and written approval has been obtained from the county office of codes and development, which shall consider the recommendations of the county board of health. Plans and proposals must meet the requirements of the land subdivision regulations of the county, and the zoning resolution of the county. 
(Res. of 6-9-1987, § 5.01; Res. of 3-14-1989, § 5.01) 
Sec. 66-106. - Prohibited discharge. 
No person shall allow the unapproved discharge or spillage of sewage, nor shall an on-site sewage management system be used or maintained in such manner that will allow the seepage or discharge of effluent from such system to any ground surface, water well, abandoned well, watercourse, drainage ditch, open trench, canal, storm drain or storm sewer, leak, stream, river, groundwater or other body of water. When, in the opinion of the county board of health, an existing on-site sewage management system presents an eminent or probable threat to public health, use of such system shall be discontinued and corrective measures shall be taken to preserve public health. 
(Res. of 6-9-1987, § 6.01) 
Secs. 66-107—66-140. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE V. - UTILITIES PROTECTION CENTER[2] 

Footnotes: 
--- (2) --- 
Editor's note— The membership agreement referred to in this article has been omitted from this codification. An official copy of the subject agreement is on file in the office of the clerk of the board of commissioners. 

Sec. 66-141. - Findings. 
(a)  O.C.G.A. § 25-9-1 et seq. authorizes utilities, including municipal and counties, to participate as members of the Utilities Protection Center, Inc., a state nonprofit corporation (the UPC). 
(b)  The county has constructed the Lake Blackshear water system and is constructing water systems in other areas of the county, and is therefore a utility that qualifies for membership in the Utilities Protection Center, Inc. 
(c)  The board of commissioners has investigated the benefits of membership in the Utilities Protection Center, Inc., and has determined that such membership would be beneficial to the county. 
(Res. of 2-9-1999(1)) 
Sec. 66-142. - Membership. 
The county shall become a member of the Utilities Protection Center, Inc., upon the terms and conditions set forth in the membership agreement attached to this article and incorporated by this reference. 
(Res. of 2-9-1999(1)) 
Sec. 66-143. - Execution of membership agreement. 
The chairman or vice-chairman is authorized to execute and deliver a membership agreement on behalf of the county. 
(Res. of 2-9-1999(1)) 
Sec. 66-144. - Attestation and sealing. 
The county administrator is authorized to affix the seal of the county to any writings executed by the chairman in connection with this article, and to attest the same, but such attestation and/or sealing is not required to evidence the same as the act and deed of the county. 
(Res. of 2-9-1999(1)) 
Secs. 66-145—66-165. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE VI. - OUTDOOR WATER USE[3] 

Footnotes: 
--- (3) --- 
Editor's note— Ord. of 12-14-2010, Arts. I—VII, was not specifically amendatory. For purposes of classification, and at the editor's discretion, these provisions have been included as §§ 66-166—66-172. 

Sec. 66-166. - Definitions. 
When used in this article: 
Address means the house number (a numeric or alphanumeric designation) that, together with the street name, describes a physical location of a specific property. Even-numbered address means a house number ending with number 0, 2, 4, 6, 8, or no house number. Odd-numbered address means a house number ending with the number 1, 3, 5, 7, or 9. 
Declared drought response level means one of four levels of drought that can be declared based on the severity of drought conditions, with one being the least severe and four being the most severe. 
(Ord. of 12-14-2010, Art. I) 
Sec. 66-167. - Applicability of article. 
This article applies to any entity, and its customers, permitted by the Georgia Environmental Protection Division (EPD) for water withdrawal or for operation of a drinking water system. 
(Ord. of 12-14-2010, Art. II) 
Sec. 66-168. - Outdoor water use schedule during non-drought periods. 
(a)  Restrictions on outdoor water of landscape. Outdoor watering for purposes of planting, growing, managing, or maintaining ground cover, trees, shrubs, or other plants in the unincorporated area may occur only between the hours of 4:00 p.m. and 10:00 a.m.; provided, however, that this limitation shall not create any limitation upon the following outdoor water uses: 
(1)  Commercial raising, harvesting, or storing of crops; feeding, breeding, or managing livestock or poultry; the commercial production or storing of feed for use in the production of livestock, including, but not limited to, cattle, calves, swine, hogs, goats, sheep, rabbits, or for use in the production of poultry, including but not limited to, chickens, hens, ratites, and turkeys; producing plants, trees, fowl, or animals; or the commercial production of aquacultural, horticultural, dairy, livestock, poultry, eggs, and apiarian products or as otherwise defined in O.C.G.A. § 1-3-3; 
(2)  Capture and reuse of cooling system condensate or stormwater in compliance with applicable local ordinances and state guidelines; 
(3)  Reuse of gray water in compliance with O.C.G.A. § 31-3-5.2 and applicable local board of health regulations; 
(4)  Use of reclaimed wastewater by a designated user from a system permitted by the Environmental Protection Division of the Georgia Department of Natural Resources to provide reclaimed wastewater; 
(5)  Watering personal food gardens; 
(6)  Watering new and replanted plant, seed, or turf in landscapes, golf courses, or sports turf fields during installation and for a period of 30 days immediately following the date of installation; 
(7)  Drip irrigation or irrigation using soaker hoses; 
(8)  Hand watering with a hose with automatic cutoff or handheld container; 
(9)  Use of water withdrawn from private water wells or surface water by an owner or operator of property if such well or surface water is on said property; 
(10)  Watering horticultural crops held for sale, resale, or installation; 
(11)  Watering athletic fields, golf courses or public turf grass recreational areas; 
(12)  Installation, maintenance, or calibration of irrigation systems; or 
(13)  Hydroseeding. 
(Ord. of 12-14-2010, Art. III) 
Sec. 66-169. - Outdoor water use schedule during declared drought response levels. 
(a)  The director of the environmental protection division is authorized to make drought declarations. 
(b)  During declared drought conditions, outdoor water use other than activities exempted in Rule 391-3-30-.05, shall occur only during scheduled hours on the scheduled days. 
(c)  Declared drought response level one. Outdoor water use may occur on scheduled days within the hours of 12:00 midnight to 10:00 a.m. and 4:00 p.m. to 12:00 midnight. 
(1)  Scheduled days for odd-numbered addresses are Tuesdays, Thursdays and Sundays. 
(2)  Scheduled days for even-numbered addresses are Mondays, Wednesdays and Saturdays. 
(3)  Use of hydrants for any purpose other than firefighting, public health, safety or flushing. 
(d)  Declared drought response level two . Outdoor water use may occur on scheduled days within the hours of 12:00 midnight to 10:00 a.m. 
(1)  Scheduled days for odd-numbered addresses are Tuesday, Thursdays and Sundays. 
(2)  Scheduled days for even-numbered addresses and golf course fairways are Mondays, Wednesdays and Saturdays. 
(3)  The following uses are prohibited: 
a.  Using hydrants for any purpose other than firefighting, public health, safety or flushing. 
b.  Washing hard surfaces, such as streets, gutters, sidewalks and driveways except when necessary for public health and safety. 
(e)  Declared drought response level three . Outdoor water use may occur on the scheduled day within the hours of 12:00 midnight to 10:00 a.m. 
(1)  The scheduled day for odd-numbered addresses is Sunday. 
(2)  The scheduled day for even-numbered addresses and golf course fairways is Saturday. 
(3)  The following uses are prohibited: 
a.  Using hydrants for any purpose other than firefighting, public health, safety or flushing. 
b.  Washing hard surfaces, such as streets, gutters, sidewalks, driveways, except when necessary for public health and safety. 
c.  Filling installed swimming pools except when necessary for health, care or structural integrity. 
d.  Washing vehicles, such as cars, boats, trailers, motorbikes, airplanes, golf carts. 
e.  Washing buildings or structures except for immediate fire protection. 
f.  Non-commercial fund-raisers, such as car washes. 
g.  Using water for ornamental purposes, such as fountains, reflecting pools, and waterfalls except when necessary to support aquatic life. 
(f)  Declared drought response level four . No outdoor water use is allowed, other than for activities exempted in Rule 391-3-30-.05, or as the EPD director may order. 
(Ord. of 12-14-2010, Art. IV) 
Sec. 66-170. - Exemptions. 
(a)  This article shall not apply to the following outdoor water uses: 
(1)  Capture and re-use of cooling system condensate or stormwater in compliance with applicable local ordinances; and 
(2)  Re-use of gray water in compliance with applicable local ordinances. 
(b)  The following established landscape water uses are exempt from the outdoor water use schedule of this article. 
(1)  Use of reclaimed wastewater by a designated user from a system permitted by EPD to provide reclaimed wastewater; and 
(2)  Irrigation of personal food gardens. 
(c)  Newly (in place less than 30 days) installed landscapes are subject to the following: 
(1)  Irrigation of newly installed landscapes is allowed any day of the week, but only during allowed hours for the drought response level in effect, for a period of 30 days following installation. No watering is allowed during drought response level four. 
(2)  For new landscapes installed by certified or licensed professionals, commercial exemptions apply. 
(d)  The following golf course outdoor water uses are exempt from the outdoor water use schedules of this article: 
(1)  Use of reclaimed wastewater by a designated user from a system permitted by EPD to provide reclaimed wastewater; 
(2)  Irrigation of fairways during times of non-drought and declared drought response level one; 
(3)  Irrigation of tees during times of non-drought and declared drought response levels one, two and three; and 
(4)  Irrigation of greens. 
(e)  The following commercial outdoor water uses are exempt from the outdoor water use schedules of this article: 
(1)  Professionally certified or licensed landscapers, golf course contractor, and sports turf landscapers: During installation and 30 days following installation only. Professional landscapers must be certified or licensed for commercial exemptions to apply. 
(2)  Irrigation contractors: During installation and as needed for proper maintenance and adjustments only. 
(3)  Sod producers. 
(4)  Ornamental growers. 
(5)  Fruit and vegetable growers. 
(6)  Retail garden centers. 
(7)  Hydro-seeding. 
(8)  Power-washing. 
(9)  Construction sites. 
(10)  Producers of food and fiber. 
(11)  Car washes. 
(12)  Other activities essential to daily business. 
(13)  Watering-in of pesticides and herbicides on turf. 
(Ord. of 12-14-2010, Art. V) 
Sec. 66-171. - Violations and penalties for non-compliance. 
(a)  Enforcement . 
(1)  No person shall use or allow the use of water in violation of the restrictions on outdoor water use contained in this article. 
(2)  The county administrator or persons designated by him shall determine if there has been a violation and initiate requests for compliance with this article, by the person violating the article. The county administrator or his designated inspectors shall be authorized to issue citations against any violator. 
(3)  Criminal and alternative penalties. Any violation of this section may also be enforced by a citation or accusation returnable to the magistrate court or by any other legal means as set forth in this Code. 
(b)  Penalties for violation. 
1st offense: Warning 
2nd offense: Fine of $50.00 
3rd offense: Fine of $300.00 
(c)  Additional remedies. Nothing contained in this section shall prevent the Crisp County Board of Commissioners and the Crisp County Water Works from taking such other lawful actions as are necessary to prevent or remedy any violations; such as injunctions, mandamus or other appropriate action; to include disconnection of service. 
(Ord. of 12-14-2010, Art. VI) 
Sec. 66-172. - References. 
This article includes and incorporates by reference the Rules of Georgia Department of Natural Resources, Environmental Protection Division, Chapter 391-30, Outdoor Water Use. 
(Ord. of 12-14-2010, Art. VII) 
APPENDIX A - UNIFIED LAND DEVELOPMENT CODE[1] 
Footnotes:

Editor's note— The November 9, 1999, Unified Development Code of Crisp County was amended in its entirety and readopted on January 1, 2009. The 2009 code is not set out herein but is available for inspection in the county offices and on the county's official web site. 
Cross reference— Any zoning ordinance saved from repeal, § 1-6(10); any ordinance dedicating or accepting any subdivision plat saved from repeal, § 1-6(11); development authority, § 2-101 et seq.; buildings and building regulations, ch. 18; manufactured homes, ch. 38; planning, ch. 46; utilities, ch. 66. 
State Law reference— The Zoning Procedures Law, O.C.G.A. § 36-66-1 et seq.; local government zoning powers, O.C.G.A. § 36-66-2; conflicts of interest in zoning actions, O.C.G.A. § 36-67A-1 et seq.; effect of zoning laws on covenants running with the land, O.C.G.A. § 44-5-60; authority to adopt plans and exercise the power of zoning, Ga. Const. art. IX, § II, ¶ IV.
